Current Affairs Commentary

Development of Proper Paths for Secondary Normal and Vocational Education 26

Yesterday, we presented a commentary. We discussed the current secondary education system, suggesting that vocational schools at all levels could be established independently. However, regular secondary schools should also possess vocational characteristics and not be viewed as purely preparatory institutions for higher education. Today, we want to further explore the issue of developing secondary normal and vocational education and assess the value of the Ministry of Education's newly established standards for allocating secondary education funding.

A certain official from the Ministry of Education once made a responsible statement on this issue. The general idea was that ordinary secondary schools in our country are unusually developed, while vocational and normal education have made little progress, especially vocational education. Therefore, the Ministry of Education's new policy is to limit funding for ordinary secondary schools to expand vocational and normal education. In recent years, due to the imbalanced development of secondary education in our country, primary schools lack qualified teachers, and ordinary secondary school graduates who cannot go on to higher education cannot engage in vocational work. All of these are ironclad facts. Without this official's remarks, we would have held the same deep feelings. However, we believe that this matter is significant. To seek remedies, we must first understand the root causes of past failures in secondary education and consider the social environment in various regions to make comprehensive plans. Then, the entire nation, from top to bottom, should work together to implement these plans according to the established procedures. If we rely solely on the efforts of the highest educational administrative agency and use funding allocation standards as the primary tool, we fear that even if the authorities are extremely diligent, it will still be ineffective. We deeply feel that to develop secondary education, we must first seek a solid foundation in elementary education. The goal of secondary normal education is to provide qualified teachers for primary schools, which is common in countries around the world. As for vocational education in our country, it should first dedicate its full efforts to primary schools, which may not be universally known. The reason why secondary normal schools and vocational schools are not as developed as ordinary secondary schools is that graduates of normal and vocational schools generally feel that there is no way out, just like ordinary secondary school graduates who cannot go on to higher education. Because the knowledge and skills learned by normal and vocational school graduates are more specialized than those of secondary school graduates, their opportunities are even fewer. Secondary normal school graduates can only become primary school teachers. Secondary vocational school graduates can only become modern foremen. Although the nature of the two is different, the one thing they share is that they are not valued by society. However, secondary school graduates can become university students, which everyone envies. Once they graduate from university, although there is still the worry of unemployment, this is a matter of several years later. In these few years, they can live freely. Therefore, most young people prefer to be ordinary secondary school students who are candidates for university students rather than normal or vocational school students who are candidates for primary school teachers or modern foremen. If the government truly wants to avoid the drawbacks of the imbalanced development of secondary education, it should first determine the direction of normal and vocational education. There is no other way but to work on elementary education so that normal school students have proper and satisfactory opportunities, and useful young people do not waste their time and money in secondary vocational schools, only to find that they cannot use what they have learned.

Now, let's talk about the issue of teachers in primary schools. Primary school teachers in our country have always been known for their hardship. In the past, during the imperial examination era, only old scholars who repeatedly failed the examinations were willing to sit on cold benches in three-family villages, barely making a living as schoolteachers for the rest of their years. Even today, the treatment of primary school teachers is still extremely meager. For example, the importance of rural normal schools has been recognized by all knowledgeable people, but the average monthly salary of primary school teachers in rural Jiangsu is less than twenty-five yuan, less than fourteen yuan in Anhui, eleven yuan on average in Hebei, and only four yuan at the lowest. The average is only eight yuan in Jiangxi. However, there are unexpected situations. Jiangsu is one of the most developed provinces in our country in terms of primary school education, but nearly half of the graduates from provincial and county normal schools in the 21st and 22nd years cannot find positions. The director of the Provincial Department of Education, seeing that there is an oversupply of primary school teachers in the province, said, "I am deeply convinced that in the field of secondary education in Jiangsu Province, not only can ordinary secondary schools not expand arbitrarily, but also normal schools should find ways to tighten up." Although the situation in other provinces may not be as bad as in Jiangsu, it is still an undeniable fact that many normal school graduates are idle and unemployed or seek other livelihoods every year. Currently, the treatment of primary school teachers is so meager, and the opportunities for normal school students are so difficult. Even if we can increase the funding for normal schools from 10% to 25% in the total budget for secondary education, what is enough to encourage students to devote themselves to normal education or arouse the enthusiasm of parents to send their children to normal schools, except for some improvement in school facilities and teaching? If there are qualified primary school teachers but no primary schools to place them, or if there are positions for primary school teachers but the income is not enough to support their parents and raise their wives and children, who would readily change their attitude of disregarding normal education just because normal schools have been slightly improved? Furthermore, even if we take a step back and assume that normal education will greatly develop due to increased funding, it will only create more educated unemployed individuals.

Next, let's talk about secondary vocational education. Vocational education in our country began at the end of the Qing Dynasty, but its achievements were not significant. The reasons for its failure are: first, the underdeveloped state of production industries in our country. Except for a few industrial areas, there is a lack of a foundation for the development of vocational schools. Second, organizers do not pay attention to local socio-economic conditions, production organizations, and raw material supply, so the school curriculum cannot adapt to the times and places. Third, people in the industry and economy do not know how to cooperate closely with organizers, support the progress of vocational schools, and promote their success. Today, the number of vocational school graduates is not very large, but there is already a lament that it is not easy to find employment. According to the Jiangsu education statistics for the 22nd year, approximately 44% of graduates from senior high school vocational programs in the province cannot find jobs. Li Ximou, a specialist from the Ministry of Education, reported that graduates from vocational schools in Bengbu and Wuhu in Anhui, and the First Vocational School in Jiangxi also feel the pain of having no way out. In all fairness, is this the students' fault? Mr. Morehead, Deputy Director of the International Labor Bureau, once told officials of our country's Ministry of Education that China should run practical vocational schools and not put on a false front. His words are thought-provoking. We believe that the most practical vocational schools today are not secondary or higher vocational schools, but elementary vocational schools aimed at improving handicrafts. If we do not understand whether all provinces and cities in the country have a common need for secondary vocational schools and their environment, and rashly issue orders to increase them in large numbers, the result will be no different from expanding secondary normal schools and neglecting the opportunities for their graduates.

Therefore, we want to suggest the following to the government: (1) In the area of secondary normal education, efforts should first be made to develop primary education in order to increase the need for primary school teachers and the opportunities for normal school students. At the same time, it is necessary to (A) screen primary school teachers in various regions and dismiss those who are not very competent, provide them with appropriate training, and have normal school graduates take their place. However, during the training period for dismissed teachers, living expenses should still be provided as usual, and training expenses should also be borne by the public. (B) Increase the salaries of primary school teachers, adopt efficiency-based salary increases and a pension system to reward their hard work. (C) Establish holiday schools and short-term refresher courses to improve the abilities and knowledge of in-service teachers and cultivate their interest in their careers.

(2) In the area of vocational education, the actual needs and environment of the vocational school location should be considered separately. Except for a few modern industrial areas, the expansion of secondary or higher vocational schools can be slowed down, and full efforts should be devoted to the addition of elementary vocational schools. As for secondary vocational schools in industrial areas: (A) attention should be paid to local economic conditions and social needs, and then special courses and internships should be determined. Efforts should be made to improve existing industries. (B) The government should encourage private industrial enterprises such as agriculture, industry, and commerce to accommodate vocational school students for internships to learn from them. Needless to say, official industrial enterprises and factories should be open. (C) Local vocational schools should form school committees with local industry representatives, principals, and teachers to seek cooperation between the school and society. (D) Following the French vocational education inspection system, inspectors should be set up in each important area. In addition to inspecting academic affairs, their duties include communicating and liaising between the school and the industry, as well as consulting and deliberating on business matters with the central Ministry of Education's inspectors.

In short, to correct the drawbacks of the imbalanced development of secondary education, we should seek solutions based on the actual situation of developing primary education and the difficulty for secondary school graduates to find employment. If we do not do this and only seek to reform the standards for secondary school funding, we fear that the impact will not only fail to increase the possibility of employment for normal and vocational school students but may also deepen the existing panic due to the expansion of enrollment in such schools.

Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs

Considering Actions Against Russia 27

The Army Ministry Adopts a Threatening Attitude

Soviet Deputy Station Master Detained and on Hunger Strike

Russian Residents in the China Eastern Railway Area Return Home

(Tokyo) According to a statement made today by a spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Japanese government is currently considering issuing a general warning to Soviet Russia, but no decision has yet been made. This warning will mention border incidents and provocative acts by Soviet Russia but will not contain any use of force. Soviet Russia is now propagating that Japan intends to occupy the China Eastern Railway, but it dares to guarantee that Japan has no such intention. The Soviet claim that Japan wants to occupy the railway because the authorities of (Manchukuo) arrested Soviet employees of the China Eastern Railway is completely unfounded. The arrest of employees of the China Eastern Railway is purely an affair of independent (Manchukuo) and has nothing to do with the transfer negotiations of the China Eastern Railway. The Japanese government now believes that these negotiations are still in progress and have not broken down. The spokesman also said that a total of seventeen employees of the China Eastern Railway have been arrested. (17th Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Army Ministry issued a public statement today, listing thirteen incidents that occurred in the eastern section of the China Eastern Railway from April to July to prove the justification for the arrest of seventeen employees of the China Eastern Railway. The statement said that an investigation has revealed that the accidents involving Japanese military trains and trains transporting military supplies were caused by the Soviet Far Eastern Army issuing orders to the Soviet employees and organizations of the China Eastern Railway, who then ordered (bandits) to attack. It also stated that the (Man) government will continue to work harder to eliminate anti-(Man) elements in the China Eastern Railway. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Japanese Army authorities are taking a positive attitude toward the numerous unpleasant incidents caused by the Soviet Union in the (Manchukuo) territory in order to fully resolve various important outstanding issues between the two countries. However, the recent intensified propaganda by the Russian side to defame Japan to various countries is likely to cause misunderstandings among the countries. Therefore, the Army authorities have decided to abandon their passive attitude and deal with Soviet Russia. The Army Ministry also advocates that Japan should disengage from all relations with the Russian-Manchukuo China Eastern Railway negotiations. (17th Dispatch)

News from Boli and Harbin: Mr. Xu Luom, the Soviet deputy station master of Harbin, was arrested without cause a month ago and is now using hunger strikes to protest this action and demand a prompt investigation of this case. Mr. Xu became extremely weak and seriously ill after six days of hunger strike, so he was moved from prison to a hospital for treatment. However, his physical condition is worrying. (16th Tass Dispatch)

(Harbin) According to reports, more than 1,500 Soviet Russian residents from Yimianpo, Muling, Wuzhan, Qiqihar, Boketu, and Manchuli have recently returned to their country. The Russian residents in the eastern and western sections of the China Eastern Railway are now only the employees of the railway. (5th Reuters Correspondence)

Endlessly Growing Japanese-Russian Disputes 28

Provocation by the Japanese Military Delegation

Boli received a message from here that a moving and sensational message has appeared in the Harbin newspapers, namely accusations of provocations against the Soviet Consulate in Suifenhe Station. The message falsely accuses the consulate and Consul Stedmatch personally of organizing armed personnel to attack the Japanese military delegation in Suifenhe Station and assassinating a White Russian guard of the delegation during this attack in March of this year. The message indicated that the attacks by these provocateurs were initially not limited to the China Eastern Railway and planned to make more serious provocations against the Soviet Consulate in Suifenhe Station. According to Harbin residents familiar with current affairs, there is now solid evidence to prove that the above-mentioned provocative message was instigated by the Japanese military delegation in Harbin. (17th Tass Dispatch)

Boli received a message from Harbin that the Police Department has issued a new order restricting the transaction of (Puche). So-called Puche are vehicles attached to trains that are equipped like shops, and their function on the road has existed for many years. This new method by the Manchurian authorities is also nothing more than an attempt to prevent the China Eastern Railway from carrying out routine work. If there are no Puche, the road workers and Soviet Russian people scattered near the small stations on the road have no way to live because there are no other facilities to provide living materials in the area. Therefore, they are now in a very difficult situation. (16th Tass Dispatch)

Recently, they have been arrested by the police in Manchuli. (8) Two Manchu hunters were arrested by the secret police while hunting near Manchuli on May 18, and only one was released. (17th Electrically Transmitted)

France and Russia Actively Unite 30

Herriot Praises the Soviet Union's Peaceful Policies

Herriot, the former French Prime Minister and current Mayor of Lyon, hosted a banquet to welcome the Soviet Russian aviators. In his welcome speech, Mr. Herriot said, "We are extremely impressed by the excellence of Soviet Russian aircraft and the confidence and precision of Soviet Russian pilots during their flights. Today, we have been able to understand the power of Soviet Russian aviation. However, the factor of this power is only a part of the greatness of the Soviet Russian people. What is more important and the source of Soviet Russian power is the sincere efforts of the Soviet Russian people to strive for peace. I remember Litvinov's words that peace is the supreme well-being of the people. I firmly believe that only this kind of regime, with the masses as its background and expressing the hopes of the masses, can sincerely strive for peace, and only this kind of regime can defend its people and prevent them from being destroyed and invaded. I wish that France and the Soviet Union can have closer and more friendly relations."

Rosenberg, the Soviet Chargé d'Affaires in France, then rose to deliver a reply, saying, "The understanding between France and the Soviet Union has a large foundation. Both countries are dedicated to peace. At the same time, their close cooperation in various aspects is a strong guarantee of peace in Europe itself. The strong welcome from all levels of France and the press to the Soviet Russian aviators proves the true meaning of this trip by the Soviet Russian aviators. Mr. Herriot believes that only a government like the Soviet Russian government, which is produced by a powerful mass movement, can implement a policy that expresses its sincere and profound efforts to strive for peace. I share these feelings. At the same time, adventure groups that isolate the masses can only engage in criminal activities, trying to sacrifice the safety and peace of the people of various European countries to resolve their internal contradictions." Afterwards, the leader of the Soviet Russian flight group, Ensign Ensilito, rose and said, "The Soviet Russian people have struggled hard to obtain their right to devote themselves to peaceful labor. Therefore, they will go all out to consolidate peace. This can be proven by our trip. The French people are very willing to have peace. We already know this deeply. Last year, French aviators led by the Minister of Aviation made a special trip to our country to prove this point." When the Soviet Russian flight group left the banquet hall, the crowd shouted "Long live Soviet Russian aviation" to welcome them. (16th Tass Dispatch)

Japanese Government Attention 31

The Theory of a Franco-Russian Military Alliance

(Tokyo) Regarding the news that France and Russia signed a military alliance in August, the Japanese government believes that it is a misrepresentation of the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty and believes that this matter is an unsettling event in the international community. The political alliances that exist now between European countries are the isolation policy of France and Russia against Germany and the policy of the Soviet Russia to ensure its territory in the Far East, the Eastern European Locarno Pact, and the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty. If such a Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Treaty is formally established, the Soviet Union will have no need to be vigilant on its western border, and there is no doubt that it will take a tough attitude towards Japan and Manchukuo in the East in the future. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Army are paying close attention to the attitude of the Soviet Union. (17th Japan Alliance Dispatch)

Statement by the French Authorities 32

Alliance with Russia is Not a Fact

(Paris) A certain American news agency released a message abroad stating that if Germany and Poland refuse to join the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact before the end of the month, France will sign a defensive military treaty with Soviet Russia. This kind of message is not in accordance with the facts. Germany and Poland have not yet responded to the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. No predictions can be made before the two countries have formally expressed their opinions. According to responsible parties, after the recent unavoidable war of words in the newspapers, it seems that Germany and Poland have a better understanding of the benefits of joining the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. This can be seen from various signs. Paris and Moscow have resolved to sign a Russian-French alliance treaty on the eve of Soviet Russia's joining the League of Nations. The fact that France is loyal to the League of Nations and abides by the spirit on which the League is based is known to everyone, and the alliance policy has long been rejected by international public opinion. In this situation, even if Germany and Poland refuse to join the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact as the American news agency predicts, we cannot imagine that Russia and France will conclude an alliance. (16th Havas Dispatch)

Finland's Ambition Against Russia 33

Hoping for War Between Japan and Russia to Invade From Within

(Moscow) The Finnish press is currently launching a campaign hoping for the outbreak of war between the Soviet Union and Japan in order to complete its invasion from within. This news only makes readers in the Soviet Union and other countries who have not yet lost their sense of humor smile. Large-scale organizational work is currently underway within Finland to realize Finland's aggressive (national mission) at the appropriate time. (The enemy is in the East) This is the official (but sometimes concealed due to diplomatic requirements) and sometimes public slogan of Finnish policy. (For several years, the Soviet Union has been appealing to the Finnish authorities to establish a sincere neighborly and peaceful relationship. Even today, this is still the case. However, they have not accepted the hand of the Soviet Union. On the contrary, they are trying to hold the hand extended from the (remote islands) hanging high over the heads of 17,000 people in the Soviet Union. This is indeed a fact. The Finnish reaction is based on its heartfelt desire for the failure of the Soviet Union to realize its national mission." (15th Havas Dispatch)

Japanese Navy Countermeasures 34

Three Ministers Discuss Separately

(Tokyo) At present, the great powers are painstakingly studying countermeasures for the 1935 naval conference. Therefore, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs will also call its ambassador to the United States, Saito, its ambassador to France, Sato, and other ambassadors and ministers back from various European and American countries to explore the true situation of various countries and study their countermeasures. Now that the opening date of the preparatory negotiations is gradually approaching, Foreign Minister Hirota met with the Prime Minister on the morning of the 17th before the cabinet meeting, reported in detail on the intentions of various countries on the naval disarmament issue, and discussed Japan's policy and various opinions for 30 minutes. Prime Minister Okada also believed that the Foreign Minister's opinion was very important, so he met with Navy Minister Osumi at 10:30 on the morning of the same day, relayed the Foreign Minister's report, and discussed the notification period for the abolition of the Washington and London treaties and other important situations until 11 o'clock. It is noteworthy that the results of this three-minister meeting will have a significant meaning in determining the disarmament countermeasures. (17th Japan League Dispatch)

No Political Interference by Japanese Residents Allowed 35

(Dalian) The Kwantung Government and the Dalian Chamber of Commerce are mainly advocating for the retention of the colonial administrative system. Now, they have begun to ask the public to assist in opposing the proposal to reorganize the Japanese army in Manchuria. The Japanese embassy in Changchun is currently not taking sides, and the economic circles have suffered greatly as a result of this dispute because capitalists are afraid to invest in Manchuria until this dispute is resolved. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

Soviet Union and the Ethnic Minorities of the Far North 36

(TASS, Moscow, July 16th) The Soviet Union has a large number of scattered ethnic minorities in the North. Their villages are scattered across an area of 15,000 kilometers, from Lapland in the west to the Bering Strait in the east, and south to the Manchurian border. There are 25 ethnic groups, totaling about 150,000 people. Some groups have fewer than a thousand adult males. These people are known as the Lopar, Nenets, Ostyak, Tungus, Chukchi, Koryak, Kamchadal, and Gilyak, among others. They are considered experts in reindeer husbandry and sled dog training and their fishing and hunting skills are comparable to those of civilized people. Their fishing rights have long been exploited by European and American whalers. They were once conquered by the Russian Cossacks, and Moscow merchants exchanged cheap calico, tobacco, and inferior wine for their valuable sable and other furs. Imperial Russian officials imposed exorbitant taxes, and the natives inevitably suffered from cold and hunger. The eternal glory of the Soviet regime in this region lies in guiding them onto the path of civilization. During the Imperial Russian era, there were only a few church schools in the area. Now there are 286 schools, with students accounting for 55% of school-age children. In 1933, the school budget was 2.6 million rubles. There are now 53 clubs, 186 reading rooms, and 87 mobile cinemas. There are also so-called cultural base camps, which are complete towns with schools providing meals, permanent hospitals, factories, veterinary stations, museums, experimental breeding grounds, and complete district Soviets. There are 12 such cultural base camps, and six more are currently being built. Sixteen languages now have alphabets, and the literacy rate has increased tenfold. Newspapers are published in local languages. Previously, the sick were always treated by witch doctors, but now there are many hospitals. The area is divided into several ethnic regions, including nine ethnic provinces and seventy-seven ethnic districts. There are 462 Soviets that have been established, and their work is closely related to the Northern Committee in Moscow. National universities have been established in Khabarovsk, Yeniseysk, and Naryan-Mar, and the famous Institute of the Peoples of the North is located in Leningrad. The Northern ethnic groups are extremely grateful for the efforts of the Soviet government. They strongly support the Frangodan Soviet settlement and actively assisted in the rescue of the Chelyuskin crew. In short, the progress of these ethnic groups in the last twenty years has exceeded twenty centuries, as they have jumped from the primitive communist society of the early Stone Age into a socialist society.

Hindenburg's Will

Causing Outside Suspicion 37

Papen Dispels It

(Berlin) According to the German News Agency, when Deputy Chancellor Papen was asked about his opinion on the August 19th plebiscite, Papen replied, "During this period of national mourning, when the entire country is mourning the late President, those who hate our country are constantly speculating about Hindenburg's will, claiming that the National Socialist Party once declared that it would never be released, but now it has suddenly been revealed. I personally delivered this will to Hitler in order to dispel the doubts of the world. The best way to do this is for Hitler to immediately make this eternally memorable document public, without hesitation, which is the most reliable evidence of his loyalty and continuing the legacy of the late President. The main point of the will is that the late President wished to see the internal unity of the entire German nation consolidated. This unity was Hindenburg's unwavering goal until his last breath, and Hitler has already put it into practice on January 30, 1933. Germany's ability to fulfill its historical mission depends on this. Hitler's only wish is to fulfill the last wish of the late President. If we want to achieve this, there is no other way than to unite and follow Hitler, remaining steadfast in this goal."

(Havas, July 16th) (Paris) Since the publication of the political will of the late German President Hindenburg, French newspapers have published detailed accounts of the important parts. The newspapers believe that the publication of this important document has a major impact on the upcoming plebiscite and is particularly beneficial to Chancellor Hitler's succession to the presidency. However, at the same time, many newspapers doubt whether the document was actually written by Hindenburg. For example, the Echo de Paris believes that the first part of the will is dated 1919, so there is no doubt about its authenticity. However, as a whole, the document is actually a supreme piece of propaganda under Hitler's rule. The Paris Daily expresses doubt about the origin of the second section of the document, but its conclusion is that the former president did acknowledge the value of Hitler's work. The Petit Journal states that it is impossible to determine the authenticity of the document at this time, but the document can indicate Hindenburg's political achievements and what history will see in the future. In addition, the Paysan de Paris does not doubt the authenticity of the document, and states that the document is actually a testament to Hindenburg's loyalty to the old Prussian spirit.

(Agence Nationale, July 16th) (London) Since the publication of the political will of the late German President Hindenburg, London newspapers have commented on it. The Times today published a Berlin dispatch stating that the publication of the will, only three days before Sunday's plebiscite, shows that its purpose is to encourage national voting, so that those who have not yet decided whether to support Hitler will also vote in favor of Hitler's position as head of state. The Daily Telegraph states that the timing of the document's publication is a propaganda masterpiece. The Daily Express, in a mocking tone, states that the long-lost document has now suddenly been found. The Daily Herald expresses doubt about the reliability of the document's origin.

(Agence Nationale, July 16th)

American Drought 41

(Washington) Government authorities today stated that the drought in the Midwest has completely withered the autumn harvest and pastures. Although there have been blessed rains of one to three inches in various places in recent days, it is too late and of little benefit to agricultural production. Only a small portion can be salvaged. Agriculture Secretary Wallace stated that there is no problem with the food supply for next year, but livestock feed will be greatly insufficient. Therefore, the issue of livestock feed relief will be given special study immediately. Officials at the Agricultural Adjustment Administration stated today that the U.S. wheat crop will be reduced in export quantity due to insufficient harvest. According to official estimates, the export volume this year will be approximately 15 million dan, but the Agricultural Adjustment Administration believes that there may not be this surplus available for export. The financial community is eagerly awaiting the White House to make another statement on the attitude towards grain speculation. According to the Department of Labor, the food index has already increased significantly, up 11% from the same day last year.

Resolves to Hold a General Strike 42

(New York) News tonight, the annual meeting of the National Textile Workers Union has resolved to hold a general strike of textile workers nationwide. This means that all textile factories in the United States will be closed within two weeks. Almost all of the representatives attending the meeting approved the proposal, which was immediately submitted to the union's executive committee for implementation and announcement before September 1st. The reason for the strike is to demand increased wages and better working conditions. The union's president, McMahon, declared this afternoon that the executive committee will proceed in accordance with the resolution of the general meeting. It is estimated that the union has a total of 300,000 members. After the strike, 200,000 non-union workers will also hold a sympathy strike. It is said that tonight's discussion by the executive committee is only a formality.

President Miklas only mentioned that Germany and Austria have the same language and the same culture. In addition, one point is particularly noteworthy: when President Miklas mentioned Germany and Austria, he used the phrase "two countries." As we expected, this phrase was used no less than three times in the speech, while Papen only referred to Germany and Austria as "two places," sometimes as countries, sometimes as places. The two contrast with each other, which is quite interesting.

United States Unifies Territory Management 50

(Washington) Renowned journalist Gruening has been appointed as the Director of the Overseas Territories Office of the Department of the Interior. Gruening is known for his familiarity with the situation in South America. In the future, he will manage Alaska, Hawaii, the Virgin Islands, and other territories, but the Philippines is not included. Before the Philippines becomes fully independent, it will be under the jurisdiction of the Department of War. Gruening was born in New York in 1887, graduated from Harvard University in 1907, and received a medical degree from Harvard in 1912. While in medical school, Gruening also studied journalism. In 1911, he was a reporter and special correspondent for the Boston American. After a year, he left and became the assistant editor of the Boston Daily. In 1914, he became the editor of the Boston Traveler. In 1916, he left the Traveler and became the editor of the Boston Daily. When the United States entered the European War, Gruening was summoned to Washington to assist in organizing the wartime Commerce Committee. After the task was completed, he returned to be the editor of the New York Tribune. However, as the war on the front lines was in full swing, he resigned from the position of editor in 1918 and joined the field artillery. After the peace was concluded, he returned to journalism. In 1927, he founded the Portland Evening News, and has been the editor of the newspaper until now.

(Agence Nationale, July 16th)

Japanese Actively Completing Manchurian-Mongolian Policy 94

Dispatching Personnel to Investigate the Products of the Xilin Gol and Ulanqab Leagues in Inner Mongolia; Planting 300,000 Mu of Opium in Kailu, Northern Rehe

(Beiping Correspondence) After Japan annexed the four northeastern provinces, it revised Tanaka's Manchurian-Mongolian policy and planned to complete its control over Manchuria and Mongolia first before carrying out other conspiracies. A certain Mongolian notable residing in Beiping received a telegram from Bailingmiao today (16th) stating that recently, large numbers of Japanese have been discovered traveling from Rehe to the Xilin Gol League and the Ulanqab League under the guise of tourism, investigating the systems, tax revenues, and general living conditions of each league and banner. Their intentions are unclear. The Japanese each carry maps, binoculars, cameras, and notebooks, and three of them are carrying surveying equipment. Because the Xilin Gol League is located in western Rehe and is an important league and banner in northern Chahar, its youth have a relatively high level of education, and its princes also have considerable influence. Furthermore, because the Ulanqab League is located in northern Suiyuan and includes four departments and six banners, it is an important area in Inner Mongolia. In addition, since the Xilin Gol and Ulanqab Leagues border Outer Mongolia, they can be used to prevent Russia and control the westward retreat of the Northeastern Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army. Therefore, they are actively investigating Inner Mongolia, starting with the Xilin Gol and Ulanqab Leagues. Although Inner Mongolia is a desert region, its products are very rich. The Mongolians rely solely on animal husbandry for a living, and cattle, horses, sheep, and camels are abundant. Agricultural products include sorghum, wheat, pine, fir, apricot, and plum. Among the minerals, coal and iron are especially abundant. The Japanese have long coveted this, so they are actively carrying out aggression.

In addition, the Japanese previously planned to control the production and sale of opium in Rehe. They established an Opium Monopoly Bureau in Chengde, specializing in the public sale of opium, which was contracted by the Japanese East Asia Development Company. According to a person from Gubeikou, an opium monopoly bureau organized by the Japanese has recently been discovered outside Gubeikou. According to someone working at the bureau, the East Asia Development Company recently enclosed 300,000 mu of private land in Kailu, Rehe, specifically to grow opium. This year's production is already enormous. (16th)

Malayan Iron Mines 101

Completely Controlled by the Japanese 102

Estimated Reserves of Approximately 80 Million Tons.

(Singapore Special Dispatch) Among the specialties of the Malay Peninsula, plants are most famous for rubber, and minerals are most famous for tin (i.e., pewter). However, in addition to tin, there is also iron among the minerals, and the output in recent years has also been quite significant. Unfortunately, all of them are controlled by the Japanese, unlike tin mines, where the majority are operated by overseas Chinese. The discovery of iron mines was originally initiated by the Japanese. Several years ago, a rubber plantation company operated by the Japanese in Malaya leased 2,000 acres of land in Johor (a state) for planting rubber trees. Within this rubber plantation, a high-quality limonite ore containing 55% to 66% iron was suddenly discovered. The total area of this mine is about 800 acres, and several other sites have been discovered later. Japan lacks iron mines domestically, so they were naturally overjoyed to find this unexpected treasure. Japanese mining experts came one after another to survey, test, and excavate with all their efforts. According to a report by the Japanese Colonial Ministry, the reserves of iron mines in the Malay Peninsula are extremely abundant. It has now been determined that there are about 80 million tons. Japanese entrepreneurs have organized three major companies to operate them: the Ishihara Sangyo Company, the Nippon Mining Company, and the Itagaki Trading Company. The iron mine operated by the Ishihara Company covers an area of approximately 1,045 acres, and the total ore volume is approximately 12 million tons. It is hematite ore with an iron content of over 60%. The current annual output is 8,000 to 10,000 tons. The Nippon Mining Company's operating site is in the Tugong area of Terengganu. The mining area covers approximately 1,080 acres, and the ore volume is approximately 60 million tons. The ore is mainly magnetite, containing approximately 30% to 40% hematite, with an iron content of over 60%. The current annual output is 300,000 to 400,000 tons, and it is expected to increase to 600,000 to 700,000 tons next year. The Itagaki Company's operating site is at the Baitun station in Kedah. It is hematite ore with an iron content of 60%, and the ore volume is approximately 5 million tons. Most of the ore produced by the three companies is sold to the Nippon Steel Corporation, with a price of 10 Straits dollars per ton, which can generate a profit of about 2-3 yuan. The Nippon Steel Corporation then transports the ore back to Japan for smelting. Because the Malay Peninsula lacks coal, and Japan is closer to this area than European countries, the iron mines of the Malay Peninsula have no choice but to be completely controlled by the Japanese.

Northwest Inspection Report by Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya 107

Present Situation in Qinghai

Qinghai is named after the Qinghai Lake (lit. Blue Sea), situated in the upper reaches of the rivers. It borders Gansu to the northeast, Xinjiang to the northwest, and Sichuan, Xikang, and Tibet to the south. The province has a total area of 2,562,500 square miles (according to the Qinghai Provincial Department of Civil Affairs) and a population of approximately 6.2 million. In ancient times, it was the land of the Western Qiang. Its rise and fall have been inconsistent throughout history, and its names have varied. During the Qing dynasty, the Xining Prefecture and various Mongol and Tibetan tribes were established, and in the early Republic of China, the Ninghai Garrison Commander was established, all under the jurisdiction of Gansu. After the establishment of the province in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), only the original seven counties under the jurisdiction of the former Xining Prefecture were included: Xining, Nianbo (now Ledu and Minhe counties), Datong, Yuanyuan, Guide, Xunhua, and Bayong (now Hualong County). Later, eight more counties were added: Gonghe, Qilian, Tongren, Minhe, Huzhu, Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian (of which Gonghe, Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian counties were newly converted from Tibetan areas through the "converting the chieftainships to administrative districts" policy, while the remaining four counties were split from the original seven counties). The northwestern part of the province has a particularly large area. The three counties of Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian alone are in need of additional county governance in terms of politics, national defense, and economy. The current provincial authorities are planning for this. Yesterday, the reporter visited the provincial government and, because Chairman Ma Lin had returned to his hometown, was received by Secretary-General Feng Guorui, Provincial Committee members Tan Keming, Yao Jun, and others, who provided detailed information about the current situation in Qinghai.

Qinghai is located on the border, close to powerful neighbors, and with complex ethnic groups, making governance extremely difficult. Since the establishment of the province, only a few years have passed, and the province has devoted most of its efforts to securing the borders, defending against threats, and harmonizing various ethnic groups. Although financial difficulties are immense and various plans have not been realized, the province has nevertheless worked hard to overcome obstacles, build up military strength, invest in industries, improve transportation, develop education for all ethnic groups, foster harmony between Mongols and Tibetans, and promote various undertakings to the best of its ability. The province has either achieved remarkable results and established preliminary frameworks for the immediate tasks that should be undertaken, or has submitted plans and engaged in development. If the nation provides effective assistance and progresses without obstacles, then the future of Qinghai holds endless hope. The central government's determination to prosper the Northwest as a foundation for recovering lost territories has moved from the stage of propaganda to the stage of implementation. After Dai and Song went west, they discussed and planned with the provincial authorities on the important policies of animal husbandry, health, relief, and economy, which have been approved by the central government and are expected to be realized. The current situation of Qinghai's administration, economy, animal husbandry, water conservancy, education, and transportation is briefly described below.

Administration

Although the ethnic minorities in Qinghai are numerous and diverse, and their customs are unique, the consistent policy of the provincial authorities over the past two decades has been to adopt a lenient approach and deal with them calmly, which has achieved a harmonious and peaceful coexistence.

Economy

Although Qinghai Province has a vast territory, apart from the dozen or so counties in the Haidong area, most of the twenty counties are swampy, cold, and barren. All financial resources rely on the income from these dozen or so counties for maintenance, and the financial situation is extremely difficult. In terms of taxation, the province relies entirely on the production of wool, which is transported to Tianjin and other places for sale. In recent years, due to sluggish sales in the east, the fur and leather industry has stagnated, and the economy has been greatly affected. (The original price of wool was six or seven yuan per dan, plus provincial export taxes, transit taxes in Ningxia and Suiyuan, and transportation costs, the cost to the sales destination is about thirty yuan, and the selling price is sometimes less than this. Sometimes it is a bit higher but it cannot catch up, so wool sales are slow. Heavy taxes and inconvenient transportation are related.) Recently, at the National Financial Conference, representatives from Qinghai Province proposed the establishment of a Central Bank of China branch in Qinghai and requested assistance from the Qinghai provincial government, both of which were approved. If this happens, the difficulties will be slightly alleviated, and it will be easier to manage the government affairs.

Animal Husbandry

The northwestern and southern parts of Qinghai are pastures for Mongols and Tibetans, so cattle, sheep, and livestock breed and reproduce in abundance, making it one of the largest pastoral areas in Northwest China. However, because the local people adhere to old habits, they do not know how to improve the breed, and they do not pay attention to hygiene. When livestock are affected by disease, they are helpless and leave it to fate, so the quantity and quality are declining day by day. If active measures are not taken, the future is very worrying. The National Economic Commission has decided to allocate 200,000 yuan to handle animal husbandry in Qinghai Province, establish a hospital, and set up veterinary hygiene institutions in various counties to facilitate improvements. The future of animal husbandry is promising.

Water Conservancy

Qinghai is the source of the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, with a very high altitude, averaging over 3,000 feet above sea level. The rivers flow down from a high position with great momentum. If there is rain, the water will flow down, and the provinces of Shandong, Henan, and other lower reaches will inevitably suffer from floods. Therefore, when talking about governing the Yellow River, extreme attention should be paid to the upper reaches of Qinghai. At the first meeting of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission last year (1933), Liu Rufan, the representative from Qinghai Province, proposed the establishment of a Gansu-Qinghai-Ningxia Water Conservancy Bureau to open canals, build embankments, plant forests, and measure and report water levels. This is a crucial plan that should be implemented without delay. As for the water channels in various counties of Qinghai Province, Xining, Datong, Qilian, Ledu, Minhe, and Xunhua counties have been operating for many years, and irrigation is relatively widespread. The province has applied to the central government to vigorously seek development.

Education

There are four secondary schools in the provincial capital, one Mongolian-Tibetan normal school, one Hui Muslim middle school, and one middle school in Ledu County. In recent years, the number of primary schools in various counties has not been small, but due to financial difficulties, equipment is incomplete. (In some rural primary schools, due to lack of funds, teachers and village chiefs have to go to the homes of students at the end of the year to collect grain as salaries.) It is difficult to compete with other provinces. As for the schools affiliated with the Qinghai Muslim Progressive Association, including primary schools in various counties and middle schools in the provincial capital, they are showing an upward trend. Recently, the Binggong construction organization has also built a Muslim high school, which will be completed by the end of the year. This is all thanks to the efforts of Master Ma, who also serves as the head of the Muslim Progressive Association, and his enthusiasm for handling education (for details on the schools under the Muslim Progressive Association system, see the statistical overview of Muslim education). In addition, Ma has also vigorously promoted Mongolian-Tibetan education, such as the Mongolian-Tibetan primary schools in Yushu County, the Mongolian-Tibetan education classes for princes and noble sons attached to the teaching department, etc., which shows his efforts in supporting special education in addition to his military duties.

Transportation

The development of transportation in Qinghai mainly relies on the cooperation of soldiers and civilians. For example, the highway from the provincial capital to Dulan, the highway from the provincial capital to the border of Gansu, the highway in Laoya Gorge, and the roads in various counties have all been completed one after another. Those that have not been completed, such as the highway from the provincial capital to Yushu and the highway into Tibet, are difficult to build without the assistance of the central government due to the long distance and the massive scale of the project.

Lu Xi

Japanese Actively Complete Manchurian-Mongolian Policy 108

Sending Personnel to Investigate the Products of Inner Mongolia in Xilin Gol League and Ulanqab League

Opening 300,000 Mu of Opium Poppy Fields in Kailu, North Rehe

Beijing Correspondence: After Japan annexed the four northeastern provinces, it revised Tanaka's Manchurian-Mongolian policy and planned to complete its power in Manchuria and Mongolia before carrying out other conspiracies. A certain Mongolian dignitary residing in Beijing received a telegram from Bailingmiao today (16th), stating that recently, a large number of Japanese have been found traveling from Rehe to the Xilin Gol League and Ulanqab League under the guise of tourism, investigating the system of each league and banner, the tax situation, and the general livelihood of the people. The purpose is unclear. The Japanese carry maps, telescopes, cameras, and diaries, and three people carry surveying machines. Because the Xilin Gol League is located in the western part of Rehe and is an important league and banner in northern Chahar, the young intellectuals of the league are relatively educated, and the princes also have considerable power. Moreover, because the Ulanqab League is located in the northern part of Suiyuan and includes four ministries and six banners, it is an important area in Inner Mongolia. In addition, the Xilin Gol League and Ulanqab League border Outer Mongolia, which can prevent Russia and control the westward retreat of the Northeast Volunteer Army. Therefore, Japan is actively investigating Inner Mongolia, starting with the Xilin Gol League and Ulanqab League. Although Inner Mongolia is a desert area, it is rich in products. Mongolians rely solely on animal husbandry for their livelihood, and cattle, horses, sheep, camels, etc., are very abundant. Agricultural products include sorghum, wheat, pine, fir, apricot, and plum. Among the minerals, coal and iron are particularly abundant. The Japanese have long coveted this and are actively carrying out aggression.

Moreover, the Japanese previously planned to control the production and sale of opium in Rehe and established an Opium Monopoly Bureau in Chengde, specializing in the public sale of opium, which was contracted by the Japanese East Asia Development Company. According to people from Gubeikou, an Opium Monopoly Bureau organized by the Japanese has been found outside Gubeikou. According to people working in the bureau, the East Asia Development Company has recently enclosed 300,000 mu of land in Kailu, Rehe, specifically for growing opium. This year, there has been a huge amount of production (16th).

Malayan Iron Mines 111

Completely Controlled by the Japanese

Reserves About 80 Million Tons

Singapore Special Dispatch: The most famous specialties of the Malay Peninsula are rubber among plants and tin (i.e., tin bronze) among minerals. However, in addition to tin, there is also iron among minerals, and the production has been considerable in recent years. Unfortunately, it is all controlled by the Japanese, unlike tin mines, which are mostly operated by our overseas Chinese. The discovery of iron mines was initiated by the Japanese. Several years ago, a rubber plantation company operated by the Japanese in Malaya leased 2,000 acres of land in Johor (state name) for planting rubber trees. In this rubber plantation, a high-quality limonite ore containing 55% to 66% iron was suddenly discovered. The total area of this ore is about 800 acres. Later, several other places were discovered. Japan lacks iron ore, so it was overjoyed to find this unexpected treasure. Therefore, Japanese mining experts came one after another, sparing no effort in surveying, testing, and excavating. According to a report by the Japanese Colonial Affairs Department, the iron ore reserves in the Malay Peninsula are extremely rich. It has now been determined that there are about 80 million tons. Japanese entrepreneurs have organized three major companies to operate them. One is the Ishihara Sangyo Company, one is the Nippon Mining Company, and one is the Hōmoku Trading Company. The iron ore operated by Ishihara Company has an area of approximately 1,045 acres and a total ore content of approximately 12 million tons, which is hematite with an iron content of more than 60%. Currently, the annual production is 8,000 to 10,000 tons. The Nippon Mining Company operates in the Tugong area of ​​Terengganu. The ore area is approximately 1,080 acres, and the ore content is approximately 60 million tons. The ore is mainly magnetite, containing approximately 30% to 40% hematite, with an iron content of more than 60%. The current annual production is 300,000 to 400,000 tons, and it is expected to increase to 600,000 to 700,000 tons next year. The Hōmoku Company operates in the Peton station of Kedah. The hematite contains 60% iron, and the ore content is approximately 5 million tons. Most of the ore produced by the three companies is sold to the Nippon Steel Corporation, which charges 10 Straits dollars per ton, making a profit of approximately 2 to 3 yuan. The Nippon Steel Corporation then transports the ore back to Japan for smelting. Because the Malay Peninsula lacks coal and Japan is closer to this place than European countries, the iron ore of the Malay Peninsula has to be completely controlled by the Japanese. Report on Inspection of the Northwest by Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya 115

The Current Situation in Qinghai

Qinghai, named for the lake, is located upstream of the major rivers. It borders Gansu to the northeast, Xinjiang to the northwest, and Sichuan, Xikang, and Tibet to the south. The province has a total area of 2,562,500 square li (according to figures released by the Qinghai Provincial Department of Civil Affairs) and a population of approximately 6.2 million. In ancient times, it was the land of the Western Qiang, with its fortunes rising and falling throughout history and various names being used. During the Qing dynasty, the Xining Prefecture and various Mongol and Tibetan tribes were established, all under the jurisdiction of Gansu. After the establishment of the province in the early Republic of China, only seven counties originally under the jurisdiction of the Xining Prefecture were included: Xining, Nianbo (now Ledu and Minhe), Datong, Qunyuan, Guide, Xunhua, and Bayong (now Hualong County). Later, eight more counties were added: Gonghe, Qumyyan, Tongren, Minhe, Huzhu, Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian (of which Gonghe, Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian were newly converted from native chieftainries, while the remaining four were split from the original seven counties). The northwestern part of the province has a particularly large area, with the three counties of Yushu, Dulan, and Nangqian alone requiring the establishment of additional county administrations for political, national defense, and economic reasons. The current provincial authorities are planning for this. Yesterday, the reporter visited the provincial government and, due to Chairman Ma Lin's return to his hometown, was received by Secretary-General Feng Guorui and provincial commissioners Tan Kemin and Yao Jun, who provided a detailed account of the current situation in Qinghai.

Qinghai is located in a remote border region, close to powerful neighbors, and with a complex ethnic composition, making governance extremely difficult. Since the establishment of the province, only a few years have passed, but the authorities have devoted most of their efforts to securing the borders, defending against threats, and harmonizing relations between the various ethnic groups. Although various plans have not been realized due to severe financial difficulties, they have overcome numerous obstacles in difficult circumstances, building up military industries and developing stocks, striving to improve transportation, developing education for all ethnic groups, fostering harmony between Mongols and Tibetans, and seeking to advance various undertakings to the best of their ability. Those tasks that were considered essential and were immediately undertaken have either achieved remarkable results and established a basic framework, or have been presented in plans and are being developed. If the people of the country provide effective assistance and progress is made without hindrance, then the future of Qinghai holds endless promise. The central government is determined to develop the Northwest as a foundation for recovering lost territories and has moved from the stage of propaganda to practical implementation. Following the westward visits of Dai and Song, their recommendations for urgently addressing important policies related to animal husbandry, health, relief, and the economy in Qinghai have been discussed and planned with the provincial authorities. These plans have now been approved by the central government and their implementation is expected soon. A brief account of the current situation in Qinghai in terms of administration, economy, animal husbandry, water conservancy, education, and transportation is provided below.

Administration

Although the ethnic minorities in Qinghai are numerous and diverse, with unique customs, the provincial authorities have consistently adopted a broad policy over the past twenty years, responding with composure and achieving a harmonious and peaceful coexistence.

Economy

Although Qinghai Province has a vast territory, most of the twenty counties, except for the ten or so counties in Haidong, are barren and infertile. The entire provincial budget relies on the revenue from these ten or so counties for its maintenance, making it extremely difficult. Furthermore, in terms of tax revenue, the province relies entirely on the production of wool, which is transported to Tianjin for sale. In recent years, due to delays in transportation and poor sales, the fur trade has stagnated, severely impacting the economy. (The original price of wool was six to seven yuan per dan, plus local export taxes, transit taxes in Ningxia and Suiyuan, and transportation costs. By the time it reached the sales destination, the cost was already around thirty yuan per dan, but the selling price was sometimes even lower. At other times, prices soared, but it was impossible to rush the goods, resulting in unsold wool. Heavy taxation and inconvenient transportation are the real issues.) Recently, at the National Finance Conference, the representative from Qinghai proposed the establishment of a Central Bank branch in Qinghai and assistance with funding for the Qinghai Provincial Government, which were both approved. If this happens, the difficulties will be alleviated and the administration will naturally be able to exert more effort.

Animal Husbandry

The northwest and south of Qinghai are grazing grounds for Mongols and Tibetans, so cattle, sheep, and livestock thrive, making it one of the largest pastures in Northwest China. However, the local people adhere to old customs, do not know how to improve breeds, and generally do not pay attention to hygiene. When livestock encounter disease, they are helpless and leave it to fate, so the quantity and quality are declining day by day. If active measures are not taken, the future is extremely worrying. It has now been decided by the National Economic Commission to allocate 200,000 yuan to manage animal husbandry in Qinghai, establish a hospital, and establish veterinary hygiene agencies in various counties to promote improvements. The future of animal husbandry is promising.

Water Conservancy

Qinghai is the source of the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, with a very high terrain, averaging over 3,000 feet above sea level. The rivers flow down from high altitudes with great force. In the event of rain, they carry sediment downstream, and the provinces of Shandong, Henan, and other provinces downstream are prone to flooding. Therefore, when discussing the governance of the Yellow River, extreme attention should be paid to the upper reaches of Qinghai first. At the first meeting of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission last year (1933), the representative from Qinghai, Liu Ruzhen, proposed the establishment of the Gansu-Qinghai-Ningxia Water Conservancy Bureau to dig canals, build embankments, afforest, and measure water levels. This is a crucial plan that cannot be delayed. As for the water canals in various counties of Qinghai, those in Xining, Datong, Qumyyan, Ledu, Minhe, and Xunhua have been in operation for many years and are generally widespread. An application has been submitted to the central government to strive for development.

Education

The provincial capital has four secondary schools, one Mongol-Tibetan normal school, and one Hui Muslim middle school. The number of primary schools in various counties has increased in recent years, but due to financial difficulties, equipment is incomplete (in some rural primary schools, teachers and village chiefs have to go to students' homes at the end of the year to collect grain as wages due to lack of funds). They can only maintain the current situation and cannot compete with other provinces. The Qinghai Muslim Education Promotion Association has been enthusiastic in its efforts. (The Muslim middle schools are showing an upward trend. The military industry is also constructing a Muslim high school, which will be completed by the end of the year. All this is due to the enthusiastic efforts of Commander Ma, who also heads the Muslim Education Promotion Association. (For details on the schools under the Muslim Education Promotion Association system, see the Statistical Overview of Muslim Education.) In addition, Ma is also actively promoting Mongol-Tibetan education, such as the Mongol-Tibetan primary school in Yushu County and the Mongol-Tibetan prince and noble education class attached to the military headquarters. This demonstrates his efforts to support special education in his spare time from military affairs.

Transportation

The development of transportation in Qinghai relies heavily on the efforts of the military industry and the cooperation of the people. Roads such as the highway from the provincial capital to Dulan, the highway from the provincial capital to the Gansu border, the Laoyaxia highway, and the roads in various counties have all been completed one after another. Those that have not been completed, such as the highway from the provincial capital to Yushu and the highway into Tibet, are difficult to construct without central government assistance due to the long distances and large scale of the project.

Lu Xi

Each County Builds Dams for Flood Control 116

Breach in Southern Hebei Floods into Shandong

Jinan Communication: After the breaches at Jiugulu Menggangji in Changyuan, Southern Hebei, additional breaches occurred at Jiaozhai, Qiangqingshankou, and other nearby locations, creating a situation reminiscent of the Shitouzhai breach last year. The turbulent floodwaters rushed northeast, passing through Hua County in Henan and Puyang in Hebei, before entering Shandong. According to reports from the Department of Civil Affairs, the floodwaters have already entered Shandong today (15th), passing through Puyang and Fan counties. Governor Han Fuqu is deeply concerned about this and has instructed Department Director Li Shuchun to urgently telegraph Puyang, Fan, Yanggu, Shouzhang, and other counties along the watercourse to mobilize laborers to quickly build dams for defense, in order to prevent fields and homes from being swept away. Director Zhang Lianjia of the River Affairs Bureau is still inspecting the upper reaches and directing the counties to build dikes for flood control. Since the breach at Changyuan, the water level in the main river has dropped sharply. Today, the water level upstream of Shaan County is 291.6 meters, a decrease of 3.43 meters compared to the highest water level on the 10th. The water level in our province has also stabilized, with only slight fluctuations and generally stable conditions. According to a telegram from County Magistrate Zhang Zhixi of Dongping County to the Department of Civil Affairs, the floodwaters in the county have receded by 5 centimeters, and it is hoped that they will be out of danger if the water does not rise again. (15th)

Anhui Province

Extending the Term of Pledges 117

Intended to Consider the Hardships of the Poor But Wuhu Pawnshops Hold Different Views

Wuhu Communication: The Anhui Provincial Government, in order to consider the hardships of the poor, has changed the rule of 18 months for pledges in the province, extending it by two months, and extending the overdue period from five days to ten days, while the interest rate remains at 2.5%. This new rule takes into account both the pawnshops and the pledgers. The most pawnshops in the province are in Wuhu, and the capital is also relatively strong. The provincial government has specially ordered the Wuhu Second District Commissioner's Office and the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce to earnestly guide and comply with the policy. However, pawnshops such as Changde, Tonghe, Huiyuan, and Xincheng in the port believe that the capital is limited, and they usually rely on bank loans. In recent years, the silver market has become tight, and banks cannot lend money, making it difficult to manage. In addition, a drought has formed locally, and nine out of ten rural homes are empty. In recent months, poor people from nearby areas have come to Wuhu to pawn their belongings, but only one in ten can redeem them. If the term of the goods is extended by two months, and the overdue period is extended from five days to ten days, the loss of hidden interest will be significant. Currently, there is a trend of not having money to meet the market. If the above-mentioned methods are implemented, they plan to stop pawning and wait for redemption. The above-mentioned opinions were requested to be presented by Tao Yutang, a standing committee member of the Chamber of Commerce, to Governor Liu Zhenhua when he inspected Wuhu a few days ago, and then the association submitted a petition to the Commissioner's Office to forward it to the Department of Finance, requesting the provincial government to reconsider the proposal and allow it to be postponed. However, all parties believe that pawnshops are the only means of turnover for the poor on weekdays, and pawnshops in the inland areas have nothing else but clothing and accessories. The pawn price is less than 30% of the original price, and even if the interest rate is high, they have to endure it. However, if the money is not available for a while, the clothes will be in danger of being forfeited. The provincial government's new approach to extending the term is really considerate of the people's difficulties. Now the pawnshops do not think so and intend to stop pawning and wait for redemption, which seems to be blackmail. Therefore, they also oppose the demands of the pawnshops, and the provincial government has also ordered the pawnshops to share the difficulties and not to overstate their words. (15th)

Songjiang

Repercussions of Jinshan's Unauthorized Demarcation of County Boundaries 118

The Fishery Association and Education Association of this county believe that Jinshan County has independently demarcated the boundary, intending to include the Jinshanwei Sanyao Beicang Xiaoguantun in the eighth district of Punan in this county into the jurisdiction of Jin County, without soliciting the consent of this county. They are proceeding unilaterally only on the grounds that the area is small. The reasons are not sufficient, and the designated boundary lines are neither natural nor clear. Furthermore, they do not comply with the promulgated boundary demarcation regulations. If this becomes a reality, there will be many disputes in the future if each county follows the precedent and changes the county boundary. All sectors of the local community can hardly tolerate this, so they have submitted detailed reasons and telegraphed the provincial and county authorities to express their opposition.

Department of Finance Dispatches Committee to Investigate Miscellaneous Taxes 119

Since the Department of Finance of this province promulgated the establishment of county treasuries and ordered each county to bring local miscellaneous taxes under the management of the county government's Miscellaneous Tax Collection Office, this has been circulated as a file. Now, in order to clarify whether the Miscellaneous Tax Collection Office of each county has been organized and established, and whether the various miscellaneous taxes are collected according to the budget, and whether there are any unbudgeted or abolished taxes that are still being collected, personnel are dispatched to inspect separately. However, the Miscellaneous Tax Collection Office of this county has been established and collected by Ke Zhang Zhao, the chief of the transportation department, who was appointed by the county magistrate as the director. Zhu Jiliang, who was commissioned by the Department of Finance, came to Songjiang yesterday to investigate in great detail.

Wuxi

Zhonghua Ship Adds Shanghai-Wuxi Freight Service 120

The Shanghai-Wuxi cargo steamship transportation originally had Gongmao, Taichang, and Xiexing three shipping companies, and the business was quite developed. However, due to business competition, fares were reduced one after another, resulting in annual losses for each company. Recently, it was agreed that the three shipping companies would cooperate to jointly transport, rectify water transport prices, and eliminate the previous competition and seizure. The Zhonghua Company, which has the earliest start and the most substantial content among the Wuxi-Liyang passenger services, also believes that the highways and provincial roads in each county have been completed one after another, and the passenger steamships have become the end of a spent arrow. Therefore, the chairman of the company, Shi Youhua Yi, decided to add Shanghai-Wuxi freight services and handle remittances, and specially prepared five express steamships such as Hengfa to start daily. The application has been approved by the Maritime Administration and the governments of Shanghai and Wuxi counties to give instructions for protection.

Dispute Over Demolition of Wasteland Dam Not Yet Resolved 121

The dispute over the demolition of the wasteland dam at the junction of Wuxi and Jiangyin, caused by Zhou Weizhi, the chief of Gushan Township in Jiangyin, who demolished it without authorization, has been sent to the Construction Department, which urgently telegraphed the governments of Wuxi and Jiangyin counties to investigate and handle it strictly, and sent Wang Yuanyi, an engineer from the department, to conduct an impartial survey. The towns of Gushan and Chenshu have successively sent telegrams to the Construction Department to appeal. Gushan Township is determined to demolish it quickly, while Chenshu Township is trying to avoid conflict. Therefore, the Gushan side has gathered hundreds of villagers to demolish the dam base and rebuild the bridge overnight, thinking that success will not be destroyed. Villagers from Chenshu Township guarded it on the night of the 6th, fearing that the dispute has not yet been resolved.

Opposition to Land Price Declaration 122

The Land Price Declaration Office of this county has recently appointed Gui Wochen, Yang Shoumei, Qian Sunqing, and others as auxiliary committee members in accordance with the provincial regulations. After Qian and others were appointed, they were afraid of rashly accepting the appointment because the matter was in its initial stage, so they telegraphed their fellow villagers in Beijing and Shanghai to ask for guidance, and the public organizations of this county jointly telegraphed the yuan road, the provincial department, and the provincial hall to request that the policy be stopped by clear order because we are still in the period of political tutelage and must not increase the burden on the people. The standing committee meeting of the Auxiliary Committee decided to postpone it for one month. It is now known that Zhang Yiu Ou, Jiang Zudai, Cai Pei, Wang Kunlun, and others, residents of this county living in Beijing, believe that the land price declaration should be held from the beginning of autonomy in accordance with the Prime Minister's Outline of National Construction, and that the increase in land price is still shared by the people of the whole county. Furthermore, for example, Chapter 2 of the Fourth Book of the Land Law (Declaration and Estimation of Land Price) has focused on occupancy estimation, and the ownership has the right to raise objections to the land administration agency's valuation and request the convening of arbitrators for arbitration. Furthermore, Chapter 8 of the Tax Arrears Regulations stipulates that within three years, only 5% annual interest will be collected on the amount owed, and only after three years of arrears will the land be auctioned, which has obviously abandoned the theory of (reporting prices are not actually collected according to the reported price) and (failure to report within the time limit is regarded as ownerless land). The methods formulated by Jiangsu Province this time do not follow the law, which is incomprehensible, and the proposals to declare in the cities of Wuxi and Nantong from July 1 of this year, and the proposals for collecting land tax, are also without legal basis. Therefore, they telegraphed Yang Hanxi and others from the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting that the citizens of Tongxi be jointly presented to the government, the court, and the ministry to strive according to law.
