Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Essentials of Shortwave Transmitters (1) 270

— Huang Jiancun

(1) Overview of Shortwave Transmitters

Currently, most of the transmitters (Transmitter) used in our wireless radio industry, except for the old freighters or schools that still use spark-type, are vacuum tube types. Considering the transmission methods of vacuum tubes, they can be roughly divided into the following two categories.

(1) Self-Excited Transmitter (2) Externally Excited (Power Amplifier Type) Vacuum Tube Control Crystal Control

The so-called self-excited (Self Oscillator System) refers to a type that uses a vacuum tube for oscillation itself to make the antenna oscillate. Generally, small power transmitters mostly use this type. Although most amateur transmitters belong to this transmission method, it is quite difficult to prevent changes in transmission frequency and output. Therefore, it is gradually being abandoned, and even small power ones of several watts are increasingly adopting power amplification.

Power amplification methods are further divided into two types: one is based on a small vacuum tube oscillator or a crystal-controlled oscillator, and the fundamental high frequency is gradually amplified by vacuum tubes in its original state; the other is to absorb (Pick up) the high harmonics and gradually expand the power. In the shortwave field, the latter method is mostly used, and all high-power transmitters generally belong to this method.

The importance of transmitters in wireless radio communication is self-evident, and the following two conditions that generally should be met must be considered in advance:

(1) Stability of High Frequency (2) Good Tone Quality

Instability of high frequency can hinder other communications, which is self-evident, and it is also impossible to fully conduct the communication of this station. However, in order to stabilize the oscillating high frequency, there is currently no other good method other than using crystals. In addition, attention should be paid to other equipment, and changes should be seriously prevented. Therefore, international coordination is essential.

Whether the tone is good or not is also greatly related to the communication speed or the removal of mixed sounds. The tone we most desire is the so-called pure direct current (P.D.C.), because it can emit clear and distinct sounds. Therefore, if there are a small amount of noise or signals of impure tones nearby, it is also easy to separate them.

The reason why vacuum tubes can be used as oscillators is entirely due to their amplification characteristics. If the tuned output circuit of the vacuum tube amplifier is coupled to the input circuit, even if the change in the current of the output circuit returns to the input circuit, the amplitude will also be expanded due to the re-amplification effect, and the voltage of the output circuit will inevitably reach a certain limit. However, if this state is exceeded, an oscillation effect will occur. Therefore, even if no voltage is applied from the outside, this circuit itself will continue to oscillate. In vacuum tube oscillators, the grid side is usually used as the input circuit, and the screen side is used as the output circuit.

Attenuation in Radios 271

— Li Yuanqing

When a radio receives audio from a distant location, the sound fluctuates, sometimes loud, sometimes soft. In radio science, this phenomenon is called attenuation (Fading).

According to the research results of general radio experts, the reason for attenuation is said to be: due to the mutual interference of sky waves. Originally, after the radio wave is output from the antenna on the transmitter, part of it travels along the ground, which is called the ground wave (Ground Wave); part of it is directly emitted into the sky, which is called the sky wave (Sky Wave). The ground wave travels from the transmitting point to the receiving point along the ground, and its distance is constant. The sky wave reaches the receiving point entirely relying on the Heaviside Laver in the air for reflection. However, the distance between the Heaviside Layer and the ground often changes (the distance is approximately from 100 miles to 200 miles), so the length of the sky wave travel also changes accordingly. The unchanging ground wave meets the constantly changing sky wave, sometimes in phase (InPhase), sometimes out of phase (Out of Phase). When in phase, the ground and sky waves help each other, and the audio signal is naturally strong; when out of phase, the ground and sky waves push against each other, and the audio signal is naturally reduced, or even disappears completely!

Experience and facts tell us that sometimes the strength of external radio waves does not change, but the received audio signal is still inconsistent, which cannot but make people shift their focus and blame the radio itself.

Indeed, a poorly installed radio or internal damage can also cause the received audio signal to fluctuate. The following are the most common points:

(1) The ground and sky wires have been used for a long time, and the winding connections have become loose.

(2) The antenna itself is too thick and sways with the wind, sometimes coming into contact with external grounded objects (such as large trees, roof tiles, etc.).

(3) The vacuum tube is poorly designed, or after being used for a long time, the cathode electron emission is abnormal, and the screen current is also unstable. — This type of vacuum tube sometimes must be burned for a certain period of time before it becomes abnormal. It is often difficult to detect by relying on the short-term test of the vacuum tube calibrator (Tube Checker). Therefore, when encountering this situation, if there is a ready-made vacuum tube at hand, it is best to replace it with a new one.

(4) Bypass or filter capacitor leakage — This is the biggest reason for the occurrence of attenuation in radios. Modern radios have a very small volume, and the temperature inside the machine is extremely high when opened. The position where air flows is even more insignificant. In this way, poorly designed capacitors are naturally more likely to be damaged. Especially the once-popular adhesive-type (Dry Electrolytic Condensei) capacitors are more affected by high temperatures. However, this type of capacitor is tested to be very perfect at ordinary indoor temperatures. Therefore, in case of this situation, it is still best to replace it with a new product using the same method as above. However, when replacing it, before determining which capacitor is actually damaged, there is no need to remove the original ones one by one, just cut off the end where it is connected to the ground wire.

In addition, various transformers, low-frequency choke coils, or speaker designs may be flawed, and the iron core is often saturated (Saturation); and the instability of the numerical value of inferior carbon resistors, etc., will also change the output volume of the radio. Here, for the sake of space, I will not go into details. In short, if you want to get good results when installing a radio, it is best to absolutely avoid using inferior products.

Design Points of Intermediate Frequency Amplification 272

— Ming Xiang

The reason why superheterodyne radios are superior to tuned high-frequency types is because they add an intermediate frequency amplification section. The so-called intermediate frequency has a very wide range, approximately from IooKC to 500KC. When designing an intermediate frequency amplification stage, a suitable frequency must first be determined. The criteria for selection are: first, it must avoid the direct capture of signals from strong local long-wave radio stations; second, the frequency must be as low as possible to obtain better amplification, but it must not be too low, so as not to mix into the audio range. Finally, because the characteristic curve of a vacuum tube used for amplification can never be a true straight line, even if the input signal voltage is a pure sine curve, it will inevitably be distorted after amplification, and harmonics will be generated. If these harmonics are within the broadcast range, they will be repeatedly input into the radio and cause interference. Based on the above three points, the most suitable intermediate frequency for broadcast radios should be 175KC. Its second harmonic 350KC and third harmonic 525KC are also not within the broadcast band. Almost all imported radios use this frequency for the intermediate frequency stage. For shortwave radios, 445KC to 465KC is usually the most suitable standard.

The fourth harmonic of 175KC is 700KC, and even the eighth harmonic is still within the broadcast band. Although they are very weak, they can also cause unexpected obstacles to the radio. Therefore, the tuning circuit and vacuum tubes of the intermediate frequency stage must be isolated and sealed one by one.

The vacuum tube for the intermediate frequency amplification stage should preferably be a tetrode screen grid tube or a strong high amplification tube, such as Nos. 35 and 78, because this type of vacuum tube can obtain higher amplification.

The number of stages in the intermediate frequency amplification section depends on the amplification required and can be calculated using the following formula: Required Amplification = Excitation Voltage Required for Detection Stage / Output Voltage of High Frequency Amplification Stage

For example, if the excitation voltage required for the grid of the detection tube is 4V (RMS) and the signal is amplified to .3V after passing through the high frequency stage and input to the intermediate frequency stage, then the amplification required for the intermediate frequency amplification section is 133.3V. If only one stage of intermediate frequency is used to obtain such a strong amplification, it is naturally impossible. Therefore, it must be divided into two stages, with each stage approximately 65V, or divided into three stages, with each stage 44V.

New Uses for Vacuum Tubes 273

— Fan Qun

It goes without saying that vacuum tubes are the brains of radio, but now their uses can be applied to almost any technology. For example, geologists use them for prospecting, chemists use them to improve their refining methods, mechanical engineers use them to control machines, industrialists use them to inspect goods, etc. There are countless examples. This article briefly describes two of its new uses. (1) Using Vacuum Tubes to Measure Length. Length is most conveniently measured directly. If the length is extremely short, then another method must be used. For example, there is a thin plate, placed on horizontal supports at both ends, and the middle section has a certain deflection due to its own weight (Desletion). If another weight is added to the plate, its deflection will inevitably increase as a result. Suppose this weight is equal to the weight of a fly, then the increased deflection is almost impossible for the human eye to discern. However, vacuum tubes can be used to measure it. The method is to use the beat phenomenon of two oscillating tubes (Beat Phenomena). This increased deflection is used to change the distance between the two metal plates of a capacitor. And this capacitor is used to control the frequency of tube A. There is another tube B, whose frequency is exactly the same as the original frequency of tube A, for example, 10,000 frequency. If the frequency of tube A changes due to the reduction of the distance between the two metal plates of its capacitor by 10.7cm (its length is only ten times the diameter of an atom), then tubes A and B can generate beats once per second. The number of these beats can be easily detected. We can use this principle to check whether the cross-sectional diameter of copper wire is correct when it is drawn. The rollers that press the copper wire are connected to the movable plate of the capacitor of tube A. If the diameter of the wire is smaller or larger than a certain limit, then the current generated by the beat can trigger the machine to stop working. Other similar tasks can also be controlled.

(2) Using Vacuum Tubes to Measure Time. The measurement of time is an important task in physics. However, the swing of the pendulum of a standard clock is often affected by temperature changes, which affect its length. Therefore, the accuracy of the clock also changes frequently. However, the frequency of a quartz oscillator changes very little with temperature. If a Lozenge-shaped quartz crystal is used, it only changes the frequency by one millionth per degree Celsius. Mr. Marrison of the Bell Telephone Laboratory in the United States used this point to create a quartz-controlled clock (Quartz Clock), whose accuracy is better than the best pendulum clock. Its basic circuit, as shown in the first diagram, is a 100,000 frequency quartz-controlled oscillator, equipped with three output circuits, so that it can be connected to the various components of this clock. The capacitor C connected to the quartz crystal can change the frequency as small as one ten-millionth of a wave. However, the rotation of the hands of the clock can never be achieved by a current of 100,000 frequency. Therefore, a submultiple generator (Submultiple Generator) is needed to generate low-frequency current. It is known that when two oscillators are coupled, there is a very significant synchronization (Syncbronisin) effect. If there is an unstable oscillator with many harmonics, whose main wave frequency is about 10,000, and it is coupled with this 100,000 frequency quartz-controlled oscillator, then the tenth harmonic (TenchHarmonic) of the former is synchronized with the latter, and the main wave in the screen circuit of the former must also be exactly 10,000 frequency, and its stability is no different from the 100,000 frequency one. If there is another unstable oscillator with many harmonics, whose main wave is 1,000 frequency, and it is coupled with the 10,000 one, then the tenth harmonic of this 1,000 frequency oscillator will be synchronized with the 10,000 frequency one. Therefore, we can obtain a stable oscillation with a frequency of 1,000. This 1,000 frequency wave is then used to rotate a synchronous motor (SynchronsusMotor). On its shaft are installed generators with 100 frequency and 10 frequency each, so that the low-frequency waves required for the rotation of the clock hands can be generated. And the stability of the frequency is similar to that of the quartz-controlled 100,000 frequency oscillator. Astronomers have said that if this clock is further improved, the difference in the time required for the Earth to rotate each day can also be measured.

First Diagram Quartz-Controlled Clock 274

Method for Homemade Electrolytic Capacitors 275

— A Know-It-All

If we have old and unused aluminum variable capacitors, we can convert them into electrolytic capacitors. How to do it? Disassemble the aluminum variable capacitor, removing the aluminum plates (if they are from the moving plate set, stack the moving plate sets together; if they are from the fixed plate set, stack the fixed plate sets together; each set can be made into an electrolytic capacitor). Drill four small holes on the edge of each plate, and insert wooden (or even better, glass) spacer rings between the plates to prevent them from touching. Then, thread four aluminum wires through the small holes of each plate, leading them out to the outside of the plates, and twist the four aluminum wires into a bundle to form an aluminum plate assembly. Place this assembly in an aluminum cup, ensuring that the aluminum plates formed by the aluminum wire assembly are isolated from the aluminum plate with insulators.

After the electrolytic capacitor is made this way, mix the following solution to pour into it:

Glycerin 100 cubic centimeters

Boric acid 62 cubic centimeters

Ammonia water 50 cc or 26%

After pouring in the liquid, it needs to be charged with DC voltage to cause polarization on the aluminum plates. When the plate is connected to DC voltage for charging, the leakage current is very large, so a resistor must be connected in series to obtain an appropriate current. The power supply device should not be overloaded and damaged. As the aluminum plate surface of the capacitor gradually develops a polarized skin, the current will slowly decrease. Then gradually reduce the value of the resistor until it is removed. If the leakage current has reached the minimum limit, then this electrolytic capacitor has been made. The maximum DC voltage for charging the electrolytic capacitor is 400 volts. The lower the voltage used, the higher the capacitance. The aluminum can is the cathode, and the aluminum wire led out is the anode. (The End)

Except for Russia, the number of radios repaired is generally proportional to the population of expatriates in Shanghai, which is also an interesting statistic.

Spring and Autumn

Records of Customs and Scenery in Miao Area (3) 277

— Jue

Miao women are also capable of spinning ramie and weaving cloth. Their looms are short, and the cloth woven on the ground is extremely strong and durable.

Besides farming and weaving, the Miao people only engage in animal husbandry. Therefore, there are the most cattle, horses, dogs, sheep, pigs, cats, chickens, and ducks in the Miao area. The Miao people raise cattle not for farming, but only for food, resources, and trade.

The Miao people's agricultural tools include plows, harrows, hoes, sickles, long-handled knives, axes, baskets, carrying cages, carrying yokes, well sweeps, waterwheels, weaving tools such as looms, shuttles, spinning wheels, and silkworm baskets. Food utensils include tripods, pots, pans, woks, bowls, chopsticks, spoons, and basins. Clothing includes necklaces, bracelets, hairnets, and clothes. Utensils include measuring cups, scales, scissors, needles, awls, rulers, combs, pestles, and grinding stones. Miscellaneous tools include firearms, sticks, ring knives, bows, crossbows, helmets, and leather armor. Musical instruments include gongs, drums, horns, reed pipes, painted horns, waist drums, and cymbals. All are made by themselves and can be used properly.

When Miao people go to the market to trade with the people, they drive cattle and horses and carry local products such as miscellaneous grains and cloth, to the market. Grain is measured with four small bowls as one liter, and cloth is measured with two hand-widths as four feet. The value of cattle and horses is determined by the number of fists. The method is to fasten a bamboo ring around the front ribs of the cattle to determine its width, and then measure the ring. Water buffaloes reaching sixteen fists are considered large, and yellow cattle reaching thirteen fists are considered large, called "fist cattle." Those with less are rare. For horses, age is considered, and a wooden stick is used to compare to the saddle position, counting from the ground. A height of thirteen fists is considered large. Fewer teeth and more fists mean a higher price, and vice versa is inferior, called "comparing horses." The Miao people generally exchange miscellaneous grains, cloth, cattle, and horses with the local people for salt, silkworm seeds, and utensils.

There are also self-employed traders in Miao villages, but rich Miao lend to poor Miao with very high interest. One thousand coins or one stone of grain can increase to several times in three years. If they cannot repay, they are replaced with mountain land and clothing. Although the poor Miao are exploited, they depend on it for a living, so there is nothing they can do. After the mountain land is replaced, they have no land to cultivate and must seek to rent land for cultivation. However, after renting land, they can only listen to the rich Miao's orders, and their lives are at their mercy. Therefore, they often instigate revenge killings, and no one refuses. The Miao people value life lightly and are prone to fighting. At the slightest disagreement, they brew wine and slaughter cattle, invite relatives and friends, and engage in armed battles, called "revenge killings."

Near Baozi Field and Zhengdaying, some Miao villages have opened shops along the main roads to trade. Merchants from Guizhou and Hunan who transport cattle pass through and stay at their homes, which is no different from ordinary inns. They know how to respect merchants, charge very low prices for firewood, water, and accommodation, and do not exploit merchants. If guests leave early and ask them to escort them, they will carry spears and protect them for dozens of miles. If they encounter Miao people lying in ambush in other villages, they will make Miao language calls. The Miao lying in ambush will not dare to offend. If the Miao lying in ambush do not retreat, they will fight with their spears, called "protecting guests."

When Miao children can walk, they burn iron stones and brand their heels and soles to make them callous and insensitive, so they can walk on thorns and stumps without injury. When children grow up, they are made to forge steel into knives, which they use for life. To test the knife, they must place the blade under the neck of a bull and bear it on their shoulders. If the bull dies immediately, it is a good knife.

The Miao crossbow is called "biased frame," which is drawn with one foot and the arrow is passed with the hand behind the back, often hitting the target. The gun is called "pole," which is more than two feet long and is used to protect the crossbow. Therefore, in battle, there must be one crossbow and one gun, moving forward together. The arrows used by the Miao people are often poisoned with hundreds of insects, so people who are hit will die immediately.

The Miao bird gun is extremely well-made. The iron tube is turned several times and polished smoothly so that the bullet is not obstructed. The bullet chamber and the firing mechanism are all well-designed. Saltpeter and sulfur are produced everywhere in the caves and mountains, and are mixed with ash from the *k'ou* tree. The smoke is white and easy to ignite. When the smoke is seen, the bullet has arrived, and can reach dozens of yards away. When encountering an enemy, they must first choose an earthen mound or rock crevice, hide and ambush, and fire the gun to attack the enemy. After firing the gun, they retreat ten steps from the bushes and hide elsewhere to prevent retaliation. The Tujia, Yao, and other ethnic groups hide in the same way as the Miao people in armed conflicts. However, when firing the gun, they must carefully observe the movement of the weeds, called "catching grass," which can often hit the target. Therefore, the Tujia and Yao people are feared by the Miao people.

Gunner Zhang 278

— Qinglin

(Gunner Zhang) is an unsung hero in the January 28th Anti-Japanese War. He was from Shandong, surnamed Zhang, and belonged to the Fifth Army. He was only an upper private, but because he was good at aiming and shooting, his brothers in the same unit called him (Gunner Zhang). One morning, when the war was raging and the gunfire was intense, the enemy was aggressive and launched a fierce attack on us. Not to mention, they were fighting under the cover of airplanes, which gave them an advantage. Although our army was poorly equipped and had no air cover, our morale was very strong. Driven by righteous indignation, we did not hesitate to meet the enemy head-on. At that time, the North Station had not yet fallen. The artillery battalion headquarters to which Gunner Zhang belonged was temporarily set up at the railway station. The artillery was also set up on it. This battalion adopted guerrilla tactics and was ordered to assist in the battle. When we gradually showed signs of weakness, we suddenly heard the roar of artillery coming from behind, and the enemy's formation was disrupted. The atmosphere had changed, and our morale was naturally greatly boosted. It turned out that two-thirds of the shells fired by Gunner Zhang hit the enemy's vital points. As a result of this battle, our army turned defeat into victory in a critical situation, all thanks to Gunner Zhang's unparalleled feat.

After that, every morning or at night, Zhang fired a dozen shots from the train to demoralize the enemy, almost as a routine. The British and American soldiers stationed in the area bordering the Chinese Concession admired his leisurely spirit. Therefore, the Western newspapers at the time praised him to the extreme. Some people said: After January 28th, the North Station was able to hold out for thirty-one days. Although it was due to the unyielding and desperate resistance of the soldiers, the biggest reason was indeed due to Gunner Zhang. The enemy's courage was inherently small, and they always tried to gain advantage through momentum, especially not being able to engage in hand-to-hand combat. They were extremely afraid of Gunner Zhang's shells, and they had very keen hearing. As long as it was a shell fired by Zhang, they could detect it, and there was overwhelming evidence that the shells fired by others in our army were not as ruthless as Gunner Zhang's. In the blink of an eye, the green smoke passed, and the enemy's corpses were lying in all directions!

Indian Asan 279

— Xianxian

Although Indians in Shanghai each have their own unique surnames and given names, they are uniformly called "Indian Asan" by the general Chinese population.

In Shanghai, at least five out of ten Indian Asans, in addition to their regular occupations, also engage in the highly profitable usury business. The interest rates they charge are usually one jiao per yuan per month, and they deduct one month's interest in advance. That is to say, if you borrow one hundred yuan from an Indian Asan, you actually receive ninety yuan, and after one month, you must fully repay one hundred yuan. If you borrow one hundred yuan and it takes four months to repay the principal and interest, you must pay no less than one hundred and thirty-three yuan.

Although Indian Asans can speak Shanghainese, they cannot read Chinese characters, so the loan documents are usually written by the Indian Asans themselves, and the borrower just puts a fingerprint on the loan document. However, the amount written on the loan document by the Indian Asan is often five times larger than the amount the borrower actually receives. For a loan of fifty yuan, they always fill in two hundred and fifty yuan. Some even ask the debtors to put a fingerprint on a blank piece of paper. Once the debtor wants to default, the Indian Asan will write a number on it himself and go to court to sue.

The regular occupations of Indian Asans are mostly police officers and doorkeepers. Although their salaries are only thirty or forty yuan a month, none of them fail to save three to five yuan a month by tightening their belts and living frugally, and exploiting our Chinese compatriots, who drink poison to quench their thirst and do not seek progress. Therefore, someone from a certain country said that Indians are Asans, and Chinese are Asis.

Going to the Disarmament Conference Su! 280

Record of Lingering Fragrance 281

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

I looked at it and often had a kind of delusion. I don’t know if the dog itself knows the preferential treatment and the importance of its position; but whether it knows it or not, the situation is always true! And I can say with certainty that if anything happened to this dog, or it was injured, or ate something bad, or suddenly got lost; as long as anything happened, everyone in the palace would be alarmed, and the impact would be far greater than the death of a eunuch, there is no doubt about that.

However, this dog still relied on the Empress Dowager's protection to have such power. Although many of the ministers residing in the capital also liked to raise dogs, the situation was, of course, as different as heaven and earth.

(13) On the Road

The train finally proceeded along the Beijing-Fengtian Line. We, eight female officials, together with Zhang De, and his gang of eunuchs, stood beside the Empress Dowager like wooden puppets sculpted in a temple. Everyone was excited, ready to admire the various wonders of this long journey: but no one dared to show a trace of excitement on their faces, not even daring to look out of the window, as if nothing had happened. Our car departed around four o'clock in the afternoon, and the first stop was Fengtai. Fengtai is only eleven kilometers away from Beijing, equivalent to a flag station of Beijing Station. Our train, in this short distance, paced forward slowly like an ox; even though it was driving so slowly, we still dared not believe that the Empress Dowager would be satisfied. As long as the car rolled a little unnaturally, she would feel unhappy. (108)

Stains on the Mirror 282

— Muyin

Rather than saying this is a comedy, it is better to say it is a tragedy!

After Miss Man discovered this little secret. The fact is this:

Miss Man has a mirror, and she always wipes it very clean every day. However, when she runs into the room for lunch every day, she always sees a little greasy stain on the edge of the mirror. She thinks unhappily in her heart, (Who is it? How annoying, doing this every day!)

However, the truth will eventually be revealed one day. When she ran into the room one morning, she saw Zhang Ma - the maid, holding a rag in one hand and a mirror in the other, admiring herself, as if sighing:

(Alas! I am already so old!)

Zhang Ma is an old woman in her fifties.

Miss Man finds it too interesting! But no one, especially a woman, wants to let herself grow old. Thirty years ago, although Zhang Ma was not necessarily beautiful, she had some virgin beauty anyway. Now that youth has passed and the traces of aging have been deeply engraved on her face, she cannot forget the mirror, so she does this every day, admiring herself, as if sighing:

(Alas! I am already so old!)

Really, rather than saying this is a comedy, it is better to say it is a tragedy!

Miscellaneous Notes

Contradictory Social Sketches 283

— Zhu Xi

▲Commercialized Education The suicides of the Peking University student organization "Occupational Sports Federation" and Zhao Wanqing, a graduate of the History Department of Nanjing Central University, bluntly show that China's education is not yet correct! College graduates from our country's top universities are still unable to find suitable jobs after graduation, and the difficulty of finding jobs for other high school graduates who are unable to pursue further education is even more tragic. As a result, a group of education experts, seeing that the situation is unfavorable, are preparing to create some kind of production education, livelihood education, and life education. Whether these three types of education can break the current bankruptcy of (graduation is unemployment) and the crisis in education is still a question. However, it is always a ridiculous and doubtful thing to expect a traditionally scholarly educator to immediately change his style and become an old farmer who personally holds a rake and hoe! However, schools do everything possible to scrape money from students in terms of tuition fees. At the beginning of the entrance examination, they first charge a registration fee of one yuan. This fee was originally intended to limit students from taking the examination frivolously, and those who were not accepted would be refunded. However, now, whether they are accepted or not, they are all confiscated. As for those who are accepted, in addition to tuition and boarding fees, there are various additional harsh taxes and miscellaneous fees. Here are some of the most common additional fees in schools: (gymnasium fee), (construction fee), (practical fee), (library fee), (medical fee), (compensation fee), (uniform fee), (lighting and water fee), and the proper book fee is not included. A student's additional harsh taxes and miscellaneous fees are at least about ten kinds, and the expenses for temporary accidents are not included. The school authorities simply regard the school as a business store, calculating on money all day long, no wonder they have no time to take care of the students' future. Therefore, I believe that in this era of advocating production education, the first thing to pay attention to is schools that are advancing commercialized education!

▲Resistance to Foreign Goods and Imports of Cosmetics During the Women's National Goods Year, which was noisy and lively, Shanghai's modern women held a large parade and rowed dragon boats to promote national goods and boycott foreign goods. They advanced on land and water, which was truly magnificent and admirable. However, in the past six months, the number of imported perfumes and cosmetics has reached more than 852,000 yuan. This break from the historical trade deficit is enough to make people gasp! Now, according to a detailed investigation, the consumption of these cosmetics is not on the face, but on two fat thighs. This really does not allow people to sigh deeply, sighing that the women's world has no conscience at all! Women who put powder on their thighs are certainly not country women who pick green onions and sell leeks, or domestic servants who carry baskets to buy vegetables. Then, the women who consume these cosmetics, in addition to a group of poor worms who sell their bodies, are those modern women who advocate bare legs. I dare not say whether any of these women who put powder on their legs participated in the resistance to foreign goods parade or dragon boat propaganda in the past, but this huge cosmetics trade deficit clearly exposes the failure of Shanghai's women's world to resist foreign goods! It is not only shameful but also painful to continue to advocate resistance to foreign goods! Alas! The so-called Women's National Goods Year!

▲New Life and Men and Women Because the Chinese authorities advocated the New Life Movement of (propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame), a group of intelligent people have gone too far. After prohibiting men and women from swimming together, they have also come up with prohibiting men and women from walking, eating, or staying in hotels together in order to win the good name of maintaining the New Life. This kind of pedantic argument that goes too far is not only troublesome and inconvenient, but even if it is implemented, if people's hearts are not improved, what good will it do for the national economy and people's livelihood! At a time when it is strictly forbidden for men and women to swim and travel together in the Southeast, Yang's daughter, who went to the New Life Water Sports, was personally driven by Chu Minyi, the secretary-general of the Executive Yuan, disguised as a coachman, to pull the horse for the mermaid, and Ms. Yang Xiuqiong went to the beach swimming pool to perform, and there were police officers to protect her. On the one hand, promoting the New Life is like this; on the other hand, promoting the New Life is like that. In this contradictory state, the old folks for men and women across the country, don't really know what the new life is!

Exchange Market Tightening Spurs Buying Spree - Supply and Demand Remain Cautious, Fluctuations Limited - Yesterday's Gold Market Saw Steady Conditions with English Silver Declining, Market Situation Recovering, and a Calm Trend Throughout the Day, with a Slight Midday Dip. Foreign Short-Term Interest Rates Made 8% Yesterday 287

The Relationship Between the Financial Industry and Time Is Extremely Close. As Autumn Goods and Grains Begin to Enter the Market, the Silver and Coin Industry Has a Period of Prosperity. Although the Market Situation Yesterday Has Improved, the Economic Foundation of the Countryside is Shaking, and It Can Be Asserted That There Has Been No Full Progress. Sharp Rise in Grain Futures and Wheat 300

In the flour market, the price of foreign wheat was reported at 34 cents below the Canadian rate, while prices in Chicago and Liverpool all rebounded. There was also demand from merchants for actual sales. Northern merchants continued to ship bulk flour to the north. As a result, market sentiment turned upward again, and factories took a wait-and-see attitude regarding sales. In the afternoon, a large outside bull suddenly bought heavily, and merchants also inquired about covering short positions. The market then suddenly soared. The closing prices were up 4.25 cents for August, 5.5 cents for July, 5.75 cents for October, 6 cents for November, 5 cents for December, and 5.25 cents for January.

Both spot flour and spot wheat were active in the wheat market, and futures wheat was sought after to cover short positions. The opening price rose by 6-7 cents, followed by successive increases. In the afternoon, large long position holders, both inside and outside the industry, bought heavily, and the demand for covering short positions was particularly strong. The market then soared again. The closing price suddenly rose by 18 cents for August, 17 cents for the following month, 16 cents for October, 15 cents each for November and December, and 7 cents for January. After holding firm for many days, spot wheat prices had slightly declined earlier. Yesterday, due to the activity in spot flour, the mills were unwilling to continue to hold firm. As a result, Fufeng and Fuxin sold 25,000-26,000 bags of Xu Zhou and Shandong high-grade wheat at a uniform price of 3.9 yuan, and other wheat at varying prices of 3.7-3.8 yuan, a price improvement of nearly 10 cents compared to the previous market, but slightly less than the previous week.

Silk and Tea Foreign Firms' Silk Sales Remain Difficult 304

(Lyon Chinese Silk Appears Strong but is Secretly Weak) As the French exchange rate rises, Chinese silk prices appear strong but are secretly weak. Although there has been no change on the surface in the price of Yellow and White Filature over the past ten days (Grade A White Filature is still at 55.5 francs per kilogram, and Grade B is 51.5 francs), when the exchange rate is factored in, the price per bale in Chinese currency (Grade A) is only 520 yuan and 479 yuan for Grade B. Compared to the beginning of last week (531 yuan for Grade A and 491 yuan for Grade B), they have each fallen by over 10 yuan. French sales of Shanghai Chinese silk remain difficult to progress.

(Chinese Silk Exports Gradually Recover) Chinese silk exports have sharply decreased. In the first six months of the year, only 3,651 bales of silk were exported from Shanghai to foreign countries. However, in the past month (i.e., July), exports have gradually recovered, with 505 bales shipped to the Americas, 601 bales to Europe, 687 bales to Asia, and 252 bales to other ports, totaling 2,045 bales.

(European Firms Take Advantage of Low Prices to Replenish Filature) Due to rising silver prices and continued tightness in foreign exchange, European firms in this port are taking the opportunity to replenish filature. As local manufacturers have ample silk stocks, they are reluctantly selling off stock. Yesterday, Dafeng and others purchased 70 bales of Grade B White Filature, and prices trended upward.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussions

The End of Hitler is Nigh 308

— Chen

Recently, American astrologers held an annual meeting in Chicago. Dr. Gordon, who (researches astronomy), declared a prophecy to his colleagues, saying that it is difficult to reverse the fate of the German dictator, and that (the end of Hitler is nigh). This is heaven's will, and was destined long ago when Hitler was born. He also said that according to the celestial phenomena, the world will be in great chaos, and only Russia will be able to live in peace.

Dr. Gordon, who (researches astronomy), actually merges with astrology, and calculates the (horoscopes) of the international situation and the rise and fall of important figures in world politics. One says that it is destined before birth, and the other says that the celestial phenomena indicate it. In addition to lamenting the development of modern social science, and the resulting decline in using it to explain the will of (God), we should also recognize that these (witchcraft cults) are attempting to appear in scientific clothing, which is completely (disrespectful) to science. However, Gordon's speculation about (the end of Hitler is nigh) may become a reality, but the reasons for it are not some (celestial phenomena), but based on the current reality of Germany.

Hitler's rise to power was in an environment of deep domestic revolutionary crisis, economic panic, and difficult foreign policy. He made countless empty promises, won the support of some small-bourgeois middle class (such as the Sturmabteilung), and ran to the position of chancellor. These promises could not be fulfilled when the worldwide economic panic had no way out, and the major powers were already brewing a major war to (redivide the world). In terms of foreign relations, the revision of the Treaty of Versailles and the demand for equal arms first encountered obstacles from Britain and France. No matter how much he barked and left the League of Nations, there was no effect. Turning to the east to develop, recovering the corridor area (Danzig), and wanting to get Russian Ukraine as a colony, he ran head-on into the resistance of the Polish government and the scathing criticism of Litvinov. The meeting between Venice and Mussolini ended in disappointment. Recently, the rebellion of the Austrian National Socialist Party did not realize the ideal of a German-Austrian merger. Although his party killed Dollfuss, it caused Italy to station troops in the Alps and repeatedly declare its maintenance of Austria's independence. All of this has made Hitler's series of national propaganda weapons, such as the Third Reich and the glory of the German nation, fall flat everywhere and run into walls everywhere.

As for domestic affairs, when (Chaplin mustache) took office, he repeatedly declared that solving unemployment and saving the economic crisis were his duties. However, the domestic economic situation not only failed to improve, but deteriorated. The reduction in national gross income, the decline in essential consumer spending, and the sevenfold reduction in current savings in two years are all facts. Although the number of unemployed has decreased slightly, it is not the result of Hitler's economic recovery, but the result of expelling Jews and driving women back to their families. If we count Herr's achievements in the past year or two, it seems that only encouraging reproduction and eliminating reproductive function are his (merits).

These events will inevitably cause the (middle class) who previously supported Hitler to become increasingly disappointed because the promises are empty, and to increase opposition to Herr. The plotting of a coup by the Sturmabteilung contains this meaning. Therefore, Hitler was forced to turn to his (trusted troops) and surrender to the national defense forces. This shows that the German government has abandoned the deception of the small-bourgeois (middle class) and blatantly fallen into the arms of financial and financial giants. However, can the rule of purely financial and financial giants solve Germany's foreign policy of overturning the Treaty of Versailles and its internal economic crisis? Absolutely not. On the contrary, it makes the general public recognize the face of the swastika flag's rule, tends to be fierce, and uses upheaval to overthrow the current rule. The words of that astrologer are probably derived from this.

From Storing Grain to People's Food and Others 309

— Yafei

Our country has never attached importance to the practice of (storing grain for famine prevention). Usually, we always plant and eat as we go, without storing anything. When the year is good, the grain prices are desperately reduced, causing farmers to suffer losses and abnormally promoting the bankruptcy of the rural economy, and the survival of farmers is also on the verge of despair. When the years are bad, the price of rice is arbitrarily raised, and unscrupulous merchants hoard goods and close their warehouses. Once a year of great famine arrives, we have to dig a well when we are thirsty and lose our composure. We have no choice but to purchase foreign rice from abroad to relieve the famine. Our China, which claims to be based on agriculture, cannot imagine that large amounts of foreign rice are imported every year, which is not to be pitied! In contrast, the small Japan, which had to buy rice from our country decades ago, now sells large quantities of rice abroad every year in less than 30 years. Their rapid agricultural advancement is truly astonishing! When I talk about the people's food, I think of a friend, Mr. Wu, who talked to me about the living conditions of the people in the puppet country under Japanese rule. One section is about the people's food problem in the puppet country, which is now excerpted below, and can also be seen in the people's food problem in the puppet country.

A few days ago, I met Mr. Wu, who was sent to the Northeast by the Commercial Press for investigation and returned, and told me some impressions of the puppet country. I asked him about the living conditions of the Northeast compatriots under the Japanese iron hooves. According to him: The people of the Eastern Province are really suffering. They cultivate the fields, but they cannot even get a grain of rice to eat. After harvesting the rice, the grain must be sold to the state completely, because the puppet country has established a large-scale grain storage to prepare for storing grain. Even if there is excess rice, it must be sold to other countries. If the people in the country want to eat rice, then each stone must be around 40 yuan. Therefore, the people here can only eat barley rice, or corn flour, bran, beans, etc. Rice is absolutely never eaten. Only those rich families and noble people can eat it.

They have at least two purposes in doing so: (1) Storing grain for famine prevention, so that the people get used to eating miscellaneous grains; raising the price of rice, that is, encouraging agricultural development, promoting reclamation, and increasing agricultural production. Even if they encounter famine years in one, two, or three years, it is easy to cope with, and they will never run out of food and cause food panic. (2) Storing grain for war, they are a country with military dreams, and are always eager for the enlightenment of the war. If the war breaks out unfortunately in the future, then military grain and people's food are so important? If they do not plan ahead, they will inevitably be flustered at the last minute. They are like this to their own country, and why not to the puppet Manchukuo, which they take care of with one hand and regard as their lifeline? This kind of mature deliberation, near worry and long-term consideration, is truly admirable!

However, what is our country like? Not to mention storing grain, there is no such thing as accumulating grain at all. Therefore, as long as we encounter a year of disaster, there is no way to think about it! Looking back at the disaster images of the three provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, the miserable and heartbreaking images are still vivid in my mind. The cries of the hungry are everywhere, and the starved corpses are everywhere, which is unbearable to see. Occasionally, I recall it, and I cannot help but feel shuddering!

Capital 310

— A Ping

Two children—the older sister is fifteen years old, and the younger brother is thirteen years old. They have no parents and no hometown.

When the iron wheels of the garbage truck rolled through this small alley, they scrambled to get up from the corner of the wall. Their dark hands rubbed their eyelids. They did not know that humans had such a thing as washing their faces; wasn't eating more important than washing their faces! Taking up their possessions, a tattered cattail bag and a pair of iron pliers, without a sense of direction, without an office, every garbage can was their treasure trove to be mined.

The two children have been living off scraps for several months.

Page 20

.

They didn't join their peers. Invading other people's territories was like being a thief. If they were caught, they would be beaten.

They said this was capital. You can't do business without capital.

Run, run, escape from the eyes of many predators. They discovered a gold and silver mountain.

At the base of a large Western-style house, there was a large pile of beer bottles lying on their sides. Within their territory, it was truly pitifully barren. Sometimes, they couldn't even find something that could be exchanged for a palatable breakfast. Now, the thirteen-year-old jumped up and said (Sister, we can eat a bowl of noodles! At that beef shop.)

Just as two beer bottles were being stuffed into his cattail bag, four peers darted out from the alley.

(Bastards! Beat them! Beat them! Beat them!)

Too late to sound the gong and withdraw the troops, twelve small arms and twelve small legs rolled around on the sidewalk.

Two beer bottles, one was snatched back, and one was broken.

Seeing that she was outnumbered, the older sister shouted (Run!), and the two children ran for their lives back to their own territory.

Sitting on the ground by the corner of the wall, the younger brother, hugging the wounds on his legs, said: (Sister, we lost money today!)

(Humph!) Grabbing a handful of dirt and slapping it on the younger brother's wounds, she exchanged a beer bottle from the cattail bag and said: (We don't do business at a loss!)

She stretched out her legs, full of the strength of a hero!

Suddenly, a stream of blood hung down from her leg, (Damn it!) Another handful of dirt.

The younger brother grabbed the beer bottle and carefully examined it.

(This wrapping paper is so fun. A ship. Too bad we don't have that kind of business!)

The sky was gloomy, without the sun. After a while, rain started to fall. They took shelter under the overpass and stared at the sky in a daze.

(It's getting cold!) The younger brother shrugged his shoulders.

(Damn it! We'll go again tomorrow!) Her legs were full of that same strength again.

(Sister, let's take more capital tomorrow—Atang, Fusheng, and that scab head, we'll beat those bastards to death!)

(Smash!) The beer bottle flew more than five feet away and broke.

Suddenly, a slap flew over, (Good boy, don't say unlucky things! We lost money today!)

The younger brother lowered his head, and the older sister glared at him.

The rain fell harder and harder!

Random Notes from the Sickbed 311

— Black Tea

I knew a long time ago that I had a lung disease. I took some over-the-counter medicine haphazardly and felt a little better. Recently, I coughed up blood, and only then did I realize that my illness was not minor. I rushed to get a checkup, and sure enough, there was already a cavity in the apex of my right lung. So I threw aside everything I should be doing and spent my days foolishly playing and sleeping.

My body has always been weak. Years of Chinese medicine as a child made it even worse. Of course, it wasn't without some benefits. To this day, no matter how bitter or unpalatable the medicine is, I can always swallow it down without even wrinkling my brow.

Because I've been sick so often, I have a deep understanding of everything related to illness. Now, I'll just write a little bit to alleviate the loneliness.

To say something without being embarrassed, I quite enjoy minor illnesses. Because in minor illnesses, you can fully enjoy the warmth of the human world. I remember that when I was at home, I would always fall ill around the third or fourth month of the lunar calendar. At that time, in our Jiang Village, the scenery was especially beautiful. No matter who it was—even my mother, who already had many children and a lot of household chores—would always take a stroll in the small garden during the long afternoons, or peer at the red and green fields through the fence. Even though she often returned with a faint sigh, feeling that life was too hard, she was still full of vitality. Since I fell ill, my mother has stayed with me all day long and rarely goes out. However, when I'm asleep, she always goes out to take a look. At this time, my younger siblings have already been sent away. She always goes to the small garden alone, takes a quick turn, and comes right back. When she returns, I'm naturally still asleep. So she sits quietly, waiting for me to wake up. As soon as I wake up, she slowly tells me about the small garden—which side has a clump of wildflowers blooming, they're purple, and which flower has fallen on the other side. Every one of these things I was mindful of before I got sick. Then I begin to understand the greatness of my mother. No matter what, she's always mindful of what her children are mindful of, even though she no longer has the leisure to simply be mindful of a clump of wildflowers.

As for my younger siblings, they are even more endearing. Because they were instructed by my mother, they don't come into my room often, but every day, when they miss me the most, they always stand quietly at the doorway, their black, gemstone-like eyes wide open, watching my sitting mother and me lying down. At this time, my mother always smiles and nods, so they tiptoe over to my bed, look at me without saying a word, and then go out again. Sometimes, when they see that my mother isn't in the room, they sneak in, and then they mostly bring me things. The most interesting thing was when my youngest brother once brought me a glass bottle filled with water and two tadpoles. At that time, my joy was hard to describe.

The worst thing about being sick is rainy days. On rainy days, not only is the air pressure very low, making you feel dull, but the sound of the rain also makes you feel lonely and sad. Naturally, sunny weather easily makes people with minor illnesses think of the scenery outside and feel restless. At the same time, the buzzing of wild bees on the window also makes your heart itch. But if you can change from lying down to sitting up and look at the gentle breeze and bright sunshine outside through the window, your heart will feel relaxed.

In addition, minor illnesses can make people think deeply. From flies to the universe, everything allows you to think slowly. At the same time, no one will disturb your train of thought. Many things that you think are unnecessary to think about when you're not sick often bring you reasons in your illness that are completely opposite to your intuitive understanding. (Minor illnesses can make people more accurate!) I often argue this way.

As for the fact that minor illnesses can keep you from doing many things you don't want to do and seeing many people you don't want to see, everyone knows that. For this point alone, minor illnesses are already worth your praise.

The Song of a Solitary Soul 312

— Autumn Moon

1. The Journey of Life

If the journey of life is one of singing birds and fragrant flowers, then you, solitary soul! Your path is as desolate as walking through a desert.

People walk the long road of life with their loved ones, laughing and talking lightly: in spring, the murmuring swallows tell them stories of childhood; in summer, the cicadas on the fir trees sing love lullabies; and the white snow of winter adds whispered words of love by the fireside. The falling leaves of autumn make them cherish the fleeting years even more.

But you, solitary soul! Do you live through such seasons in cold isolation?

You are: in the desolate desert, your heart heavy as lead, you tread weary, heavy steps, walking alone. From summer to autumn, from winter to spring, what are you doing it all for?

You are: in this solitary journey, solitary soul! Do you believe you will find a vast oasis?

2. The Eternal Traveler

Be an eternal traveler, go! Shoulder your baggage, carry a large umbrella, drag your heavy steps, wander along the indistinct horizon, to the distant end of the world:

Entrust your life to nature, let your days wear away on the journey. Bathe in the clear breeze and bright moon's dewy abundance in the evening, feast on the fragrant blooms of the four seasons in the morning. The owl guides you, the nightingale accompanies you, singing songs. – From now on, you move forward with steady steps, looking at the distant future, walking alone.

Then, you cherish the brightness of the autumn moon, whispering intimately to the horizon; you love the chirping of autumn insects, like the low, sobbing cries of a widow. – From now on, the cloudy mountain peaks, the distant and vast sky, will be your home, your eternal longing, your cherished childhood –

From now on, the days and hours pass leisurely, allowing your footsteps to traverse the ends of the earth: wandering east or west, south or north. The sound waves of your wild songs echo on the peaks of the Kunlun Mountains, your wandering chants have passed along the shores of the Mediterranean; let you gaze upon the majestic appearance of the pyramids, let you commemorate the past of Jerusalem:

Go! Shoulder your baggage, carry a large umbrella, be an eternal traveler.

Auntie: (Darling, what are you thinking about again?)

Rich man: (Yes, didn't you say how old I am this year!)

Fiction

Gold and Silver Ditch (3) 313

— Ji Yu

The squad leader stood up tiredly and stretched, squinting at the walls around the main room. Old Man Wang hurried forward:

—What do you need, Squad Leader?

—Where's my hat?

—Oh, the sun is very strong, please sit for a while longer. Old Man Wang politely tried to keep him.

—No, I can't, I still have official business to run! the squad leader said firmly.

Old Man Wang handed the squad leader's hat, oiled paper umbrella, and bundle to him, then took out three silver coins from the pocket of his blue cloth short-sleeved shirt and respectfully handed them to the squad leader:

—These are for Squad Leader, one dollar for your trouble, one dollar because I didn't buy any meat today... the rest is for not getting Squad Leader any cigarettes... it's not much, thank you for your trouble, I'm sorry...

The squad leader took the money, pretended to be serious for a moment, and then began to speak sternly:

—That's what you say, but tomorrow you come to the village and pay off the full amount... remember clearly, the full amount is ten dollars, the registration fee at the regiment is one dollar and fifty cents, and... this... this... well, that can be said later, a total of eleven dollars and fifty cents, remember? If you don't pay it off tomorrow, according to the rules, it's a fine of two dollars for each day, double the fine after three days, and you'll have to sit in the (dark room)... everyone knows their own business!

Old Man Wang didn't say anything, just nodded. The squad leader and the militiaman left together. Old Man Wang stood there blankly, as if he had lost his soul. After the bark of the yellow dog, there was the intermittent sound of the waterwheel and an unpleasant, dry cough.

× × ×

The summer night breeze brought some coolness, seeping into the hearts of the farmers, which had been scorched by the flames of the day. They dragged their tired bodies and lay down on the bamboo mats spread under the eaves of their houses or in the courtyards, and fell asleep snoring.

At Old Man Wang's door, there was no mat, and no one was lying on the ground. His consumptive daughter-in-law had long since called Xiuying away. Old Man Wang squatted alone with his back to the (ancestral altar), his hands on his knees, staring blankly at the fence across the way, thinking about what had happened today and the eleven and a half dollars he had to go to the regiment with tomorrow. His son and grandson had been drafted away, were they still alive or dead now?

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Hollywood's Work to Prevent Kidnappers (Part 1) 314

— Wen Ying

Recent Resurgence of Kidnappings and Extortion, All Parties Cooperating to Step Up Efforts to Eradicate

Not long ago, an oil tycoon living in Hollywood, named Gutheral, was kidnapped by kidnappers. This is a sign of the resurgence of kidnapping in Hollywood. The general stars are once again panic-stricken and uneasy. Even the calm Garbo, who has always relied on fierce dogs for protection, has now begun to hire several bodyguards. Many stars have once again been subjected to extortion by bandits. Among them, Ann Harding, Marlene Dietrich, Mae West, Bing Crosby, and Constance Bennett have received many threatening letters. Mae West was ordered by bandits not to testify in court because she had lost valuable jewelry, otherwise, she would be punished by (disfigurement). Many extortion incidents have been resolved quickly and privately, because many stars are afraid of trouble, and many are loose with money. Paying a few thousand dollars to ensure the safety of oneself or one's family is not worth arguing about.

However, according to the Hollywood police, there will be no more shocking kidnapping cases in the future. Because of the comprehensive defense and the concerted efforts of film companies and stars, Hollywood has become a place that kidnappers can only dream of. Gutheral was kidnapped, and the Hollywood police cracked the case in just six days. Gutheral was rescued without spending a penny. The kidnappers were arrested and sentenced to life imprisonment. The Gutheral case is a touchstone for the Hollywood police authorities' capabilities and is also related to the fate of Hollywood's general movie stars. He lives at the foot of Beverly Hills, where the villas of stars are lined up one after another. They are also very familiar with this rich man. Therefore, since he was kidnapped, the villas of the general stars have been lined up one after another. They were waiting for the people from their own houses to come back. They thought, if the kidnappers were victorious, got a huge ransom, and got away with it, then who would be the next to be kidnapped? Whether the power of the kidnappers has grown to an unstoppable extent, and whether the Hollywood local authorities have the strength to protect the stars. Later, Gutheral actually returned safely without a scratch, and the whole of Hollywood was in an uproar. The stars all ran to Gutheral's house, shouting and celebrating, and the lawn in front of Gutheral's house immediately became a place for a public gathering. Los Angeles Prosecutor Fizer, Police Chief Davis, and Detective Chief Bisgailtz became temporary national heroes, cheered everywhere. Mr. Fizer also publicly gave a speech on the thoroughness of Hollywood's protection of the stars, advising the public not to worry. Now let us record the general outline of Fizer's speech below:

(This is certainly something that Hollywood should celebrate. Hollywood is where the stars gather, and it is also the place most coveted by bandits in the United States. They think that the general movie stars earn as much as five or six thousand dollars a week, so they must be able to afford the ransom. Moreover, the general kidnappers are undoubtedly admirers of the stars, so they don't need to spend money to buy off routes. There is also the point that when these stars are filming, they are suddenly kidnapped by bandits, and the film company is willing to pay a huge ransom to protect the lives of the stars, because the company has already spent a lot of money, and the film has already been half-shot. If the stars don't come out, the capital they have already put down will all be in vain. The above are all the reasons why bandits covet the general movie stars in Hollywood.)

However, according to Mr. Fizer's view, there are many difficulties in kidnapping stars. First, the stars are recognized by the public, and it is difficult to hide and transport them. The stars have very heavy workloads and social interactions, and people are constantly looking for them, so if they are kidnapped and disappear, someone will definitely discover and ask about it within ten or twenty minutes. Ordinary businessmen often disappear, and no one knows about it for several hours, which is different from the stars. Therefore, the kidnappers' methods must be quick and clean, and not a single second can be wasted. This requires an extremely complete organization and bandits with both courage and knowledge to engage in the kidnapping business in Hollywood. Moreover, the thoroughness of the Hollywood local authorities' protection of the general stars makes the general bandits feel a sense of despair. Now let us listen to Mr. Fizer's various arrangements to prevent the behavior of kidnappers. (To be continued) Film Review

Review of (Shadow of the Knife) 315

— Hu Yue

Tomorrow At Seven - Showing at Grand Shanghai

(Shadow of the Knife), like most detective films, contains coincidence, fortuity, artificiality, far-fetchedness, and a lack of character development. It shares these common flaws with other films of the genre.

While (Shadow of the Knife) features the convoluted plot and unexpected resolution typical of detective films, the director's poor handling and the absence of an atmosphere of suspense and dread diminish the impact that even standard detective stories should achieve.

In "Tomorrow at Seven," the director could build suspense by employing various horror elements to heighten the audience's anticipation. At the climax of seven o'clock, the director could then deliver the thrills inherent in a detective story through meticulous planning.

However, the director of (Shadow of the Knife) has failed to capitalize on these elements effectively.

During the nascent era of Chinese cinema, detective films featuring inserted knives and left calling cards were not uncommon. However, such simplistic and shallow works have long been discarded by the times.

Nevertheless, after several years, the American RKO Pictures has produced this juvenile narrative for the silver screen. The scriptwriter's shallowness and vapidity are therefore readily apparent.

This film will undoubtedly meet the same fate as Westerns, failing to resonate with audiences who are at the forefront of the times.

Further Notes on Dorothy Dell 316

— Fu

This magazine has already reported on the unfortunate death of Dorothy Dell, but it was not detailed. Now I will add some details. Dorothy Dell was selected by Earl Carroll as one of the sixteen most beautiful women in the film industry. In fact, she can also be said to be the most beautiful person in Hollywood, because her figure is not only the best in Hollywood, but also probably unmatched anywhere in the world. At the age of fifteen, she won the title of (Miss America), and soon she was awarded the title of (Miss Universe). Before entering the film industry, she had already become famous in the Broadway musical scene. She had only been in Hollywood for half a year, and Paramount was already considering promoting her to a star. Unfortunately, a car accident occurred, and she and the driver of the car died tragically within a few hours. Her driver, Dr. Carl Wagner, was a doctor in Pasadena near Hollywood and a well-known figure in social circles. After the banquet in Pasadena ended, Wagner personally drove her back. Unexpectedly, at a turning point in the middle of the journey, Wagner lost control accidentally, and the car crashed into a utility pole. Dorothy died instantly, and Wagner also suffered a skull fracture and died six hours after being taken to the hospital. This happened on the night of June 7. Paramount all expressed regret for Dorothy Dell's death, because if she had not died so fast, she could have become a brilliant star by now.

The Origin of Strange Advertisements Amidst the Opening of (Song of the Fishermen) 317

— Willow Catkins

About two weeks ago, an advertisement for (Song of the Fishermen) was published in the film section of both the Shen and Xin newspapers. The few words were quite eye-catching. At the time, the Jincheng Theater suspected that it was sent by Lianhua, while Lianhua suspected that it was sent by Jincheng. Unexpectedly, when the two parties asked each other face to face the next day, it was not either of them. They then called the newspaper office to inquire. It was said that an unknown man brought the manuscript and cash to be published. The name and address were unknown even to the newspaper office. And he spent a lot of money, one advertisement cost 54 yuan and 40 cents. So this matter became a mystery. Recently, I accidentally discovered that the friend who sent the free advertisement was a Mr. Jin from Baodacanhang in Xian'gua Street in the South City. According to him, he likes to watch Lianhua films the most, and this (Song of the Fishermen) is even more to his taste. He has watched it as many as nine times. He and Jincheng and Lianhua can be said to have no relationship at all. This time, the sending of the advertisement was entirely driven by a love for (Song of the Fishermen), and there was no other purpose. Only then was this mystery broken. A movie fan like Mr. Jin can be considered enthusiastic.

Film Novel

Little Baby (Baby Take A Bow) (6) 320

— By Caoshi

Eddie and Laurel were anxious to find a safe place to hide the string of pearls. The radio—the vase—everything seemed easily visible. But Eddie suddenly had an idea—Whilshire would never search a place he had already searched. So he lifted the lid of the coffee pot and put the long string of pearls inside. Soon after, when Whilshire walked back into the room, the first thing he saw was the coffee pot, and he immediately wanted to pour himself some coffee. Beads of sweat appeared on Laurel's forehead, and Eddie trembled, reaching out to grab it. But the coffee had already poured into the cup. Whilshire took a sip and thought it tasted like dishwater, so he didn't drink it. Whilshire then went back to the bedroom to continue his search. Shirley seized the opportunity to sneak into the dining room, take the pearls from the coffee pot, and hide behind Eddie, pulling on his clothes and saying, "(Don't trick me, Daddy—I found them again!)" Eddie was almost scared out of his mind. He snatched the pearls from her hand, tossed her a small silver dollar, and told her to go buy herself some ice cream. Shirley happily left. Whilshire was concentrating on searching the bedroom. Eddie knew he had to hide them immediately—Laurel saw a carpet beater and quickly opened it up, stuffing the pearls inside. Suddenly, a rude voice startled them again, it was Annie—the maid from the apartment—who wanted to borrow the carpet beater! Laurel and Eddie watched the carpet beater leave, feeling much relieved. Whilshire watched suspiciously, shaking his head. "It wouldn't be in there!" He glared at the two young people. "(Okay, I'll spare you today—but don't think I'm giving up!)"

After Whilshire left, they rushed to retrieve the carpet beater. But when they opened the carpet beater, there was only dust inside. Where had the pearls gone? At this time, Annie was also nowhere to be found; tonight was her day off. Eddie, Laurel, Kay, and Keene searched everywhere, but the pearls were not found.

Eddie was searching alone at home when he suddenly heard a faint "(Hands up)," and he stood up. It turned out to be Stone coming to get the pearls. Stone held a pistol, forcing Eddie back until he had nowhere to retreat, his back against the wall. Stone had now reached the center of the room. Eddie used his arm to press the mechanism on the wall that stored the bed inside the wall, and the bed immediately fell down, hitting Stone. Eddie quickly punched him unconscious. After tying Stone up with rope, he dragged him into the kitchen and rushed to find the police...

Shirley, looking for a cat, unintentionally found the pearls again in the trash can. She ran back in shock, shouting, "(Daddy—Daddy—I found them!)" But Daddy was nowhere to be found. And the person who gave her the pearls was lying in the kitchen, tied up with ropes. Shirley looked at him suspiciously. "(Um, mister, your pearls were gone, but I found them!)" Stone looked up and said, "(Great. You're a really smart good kid. But please untie my ropes.)" Shirley looked at him closely for a while. "(Are you playing a game?)" Stone tricked her, "(Your daddy tied me up so I couldn't peek?)" Shirley was still a bit hesitant. But she couldn't resist Stone's repeated coaxing. So she took a kitchen knife and cut the ropes for him.

Luckily, Eddie hadn't gone far. The police had received a warning that Stone had appeared nearby, and Frenegan led the police to surround the house. Kay and Beebe arrived a few seconds earlier. As soon as she got home, she heard the frantic shout, "(Help! Daddy! Let me go! Let me go!)" It was Shirley's voice. She rushed upstairs without regard for her own life. But by the time she got upstairs, Stone had already taken Shirley through the window onto the roof. Kay's exclamation drowned out the child's cries. (To be continued)
